However, despite Imprison's similar effect of restricting move usage, Aroma Veil does not protect against it. When facing a Pokémon with Aroma Veil, Psychic Noise will still deal damage, but its additional effect will be nullified. Notably, among the abilities introduced in Generation VI, Aroma Veil holds the distinction of being the first in terms of index number sequencing.

Title: Flower Veil (Ability)

The Ability known as Flower Veil (フラワーベール in Japanese) made its debut in Generation VI. Before Generation VII, it served as a unique signature Ability for the Flabébé evolutionary family. Subsequently, in Generation VIII, Comfey also held it as a signature Ability. Flower Veil acts to shield the Grass-type Pokémon possessing it, along with its Grass-type allies (even those not directly adjacent), from having their stats decreased by opposing Pokémon. However, stat reductions that are self-imposed, such as those caused by moves like Leaf Storm or the Weak Armor Ability, remain unaffected. For a Grass-type Pokémon equipped with the Contrary Ability, Flower Veil still thwarts its stats from being reduced, taking Contrary's mechanics into account. Furthermore, it offers no protection against Spectral Thief's ability to pilfer (effectively reset) beneficial stat boosts. Moreover, this Ability shields the Grass-type Pokémon carrying it and its Grass-type teammates (regardless of adjacency) from incurring non-volatile status ailments or the drowsy effect of Yawn. Nevertheless, if a Pokémon is already under the influence of Yawn's drowsiness, Flower Veil cannot stop it from subsequently falling asleep. Abilities like Rest, or items such as the Flame Orb and Toxic Orb, are entirely unaffected by Flower Veil. Within Pokémon Super Mystery Dungeon, any Grass-type allies positioned next to a Pokémon with Flower Veil are safeguarded against detrimental status conditions and stat reductions. Despite what its in-game description might imply, Flower Veil does not extend its benefits to the user unless that Pokémon is itself a Grass type. Trevor's Florges was shown to possess Flower Veil as her Ability in the Japan Mini-volume 6 of the X & Y arc. Curiously, despite its effects exclusively benefiting Grass-type Pokémon, none of the species inherently equipped with Flower Veil are actually Grass types; all of them are, in fact, Fairy types.

Title: Cheek Pouch (Ability)

Cheek Pouch (Japanese: ほおぶくろ Cheek Pouch) is an Ability that made its debut in Generation VI. A Pokémon possessing Cheek Pouch will restore 33% of its maximum HP upon consuming a Berry, with this recovery consistently occurring after the Berry's primary effect has taken place. This Ability's activation extends to situations where the Pokémon eats a Berry held by an opposing Pokémon via moves such as Bug Bite, Pluck, or Fling, provided the Berry is genuinely consumed for an effect, which is visibly indicated by the Berry consumption animation. Conversely, Cheek Pouch does not trigger when a Berry is consumed through other methods, including the move Natural Gift, using Fling as the attacking Pokémon, or a Trainer directly providing a Berry from their Bag. Furthermore, the Ability will remain inactive if the Pokémon is under the influence of Heal Block.

In Mystery Dungeon series titles, when a Pokémon with Cheek Pouch consumes any food item, Berry, Seed, or health drink, it will recover 25 HP. Additionally, an enemy Pokémon with this Ability in Mystery Dungeon games is guaranteed to spawn holding a Seed, irrespective of whether other items are available on the floor. On occasion, this might be a Tiny Reviver Seed or a Reviver Seed; in such cases, the enemy Pokémon will utilize it upon fainting, transforming it into a Plain Seed.

In Pokémon UNITE, Cheek Pouch functions as Greedent's unique Ability. When Greedent eats a Berry, it recovers HP after the Berry's effects are applied, and simultaneously stashes an Oran Berry in its tail. Taking damage from a single attack or a combination of attacks will cause an Oran Berry to drop from Greedent's tail, with these dropped Berries remaining on the ground for 10 seconds. Historically, prior to Generation VIII, all Pokémon featuring Cheek Pouch also had Pickup as their other standard Ability.

Title: Protean (Ability)

This page details Protean, a Pokémon Ability (known as へんげんじざい in Japanese) first appearing in Generation VI. During Generation VIII, it was uniquely associated with the Pokémon Kecleon.

A Pokémon possessing Protean will, just prior to executing any move (with the exception of Struggle), instantaneously alter its own type to match that of the move it is about to use. This transformation invariably results in the user becoming a single-type Pokémon. Since this Ability takes effect before a move's execution, the Pokémon will gain the same-type attack bonus for every move it deploys (excluding Struggle and Revelation Dance when it is typeless), regardless of that move's inherent type. Furthermore, it guarantees a hit with the move Toxic.

For moves that invoke other moves (like Nature Power), the type of the *called* move dictates the transformation. Similarly, if a move's type can change, or if it has been influenced by Electrify or Ion Deluge, the final type it becomes is the one Protean considers. If the Pokémon attempts a move that modifies its own type, such as Camouflage, Protean will first shift the user's type to match the move's type. Subsequently, the move itself will either fail or proceed to change the user's type once more. Regarding the move Curse (unless Electrify has altered its type), should the user not be Ghost-type before Protean's activation, the Ability will transform it into Ghost-type. The Pokémon will then execute Curse's Ghost-type effect upon itself, ignoring the influence of Follow Me, Rage Powder, or Crafty Shield.

Protean's effect will not manifest under several circumstances: if the move's execution is completely halted and its name isn't declared (e.g., due to infatuation or confusion); if abilities like Dazzling or Queenly Majesty, environmental conditions such as heavy rain or extremely harsh sunlight, or the effect of Powder prevent the move; or if the user's current single type already matches that of the chosen move. Conversely, Protean *will* activate even if the move fails to hit the target, has no impact due to the target's type, or is blocked by a protective move.

While Protean typically activates even if the move itself fails, certain moves are exceptions because they verify their success *before* Protean can activate, thus preventing its effect if they fail. These include:
*   Counter, Mirror Coat, and Metal Burst (if the user hasn't been hit by an attack).
*   Explosion, Self-Destruct, Mind Blown, and Misty Explosion (if a Pokémon with Damp is present).
*   Rest (if the user has full HP, is already asleep, or possesses Insomnia, Vital Spirit, or Comatose).
*   Teleport (if the user lacks allies or all allies have fainted).
*   Protection moves (if the user acted last or successfully used a protection move in the preceding turn).
*   Destiny Bond (if the user successfully used Destiny Bond in the previous turn).
*   Future Sight and Doom Desire (if the target is already marked by either of these moves).
*   Fake Out, Mat Block, and First Impression (if it's not the user's initial turn).
*   Follow Me and Rage Powder (if the battle is a single battle).
*   Spit Up and Swallow (if the user has no stockpiles accumulated).
*   Last Resort (if the user has not yet employed all its other known moves, only knows Last Resort, or doesn't know Last Resort but used it via a calling effect).
*   Sucker Punch (if the target has already acted or did not choose an offensive move).
*   Clangorous Soul (if the user lacks sufficient HP for the move).
*   No Retreat (if the user has previously successfully deployed No Retreat).

The Pokémon's newly acquired type persists until it is either altered once more or the user withdraws from battle. Neither negating nor replacing Protean will revert the user to its original type. Furthermore, Protean can only trigger once per Pokémon upon entry into battle. Should the user undergo Terastallization, Protean's effects become nullified, rendering it ineffective on a Terastallized Pokémon. Notably, Protean stands alongside Shell Armor as the only Abilities obtainable as a Hidden Ability by multiple lines of first partner Pokémon.

Title: Magician (Ability)

While "Magician" can refer to a character in Pokémon Adventures or one from Pokémon Trading Card Game 2: The Invasion of Team GR!, this page focuses on the Ability. Known as マジシャン (Magician) in Japanese, this Ability first appeared in Generation VI. Upon striking an opponent with a damaging attack, a Pokémon possessing Magician will seize the target's held item. However, this Ability remains dormant if the user is already clutching an item.

Certain moves like Fling, Natural Gift, Future Sight, and Doom Desire fail to trigger Magician. Present, conversely, will only activate it if it successfully inflicts damage. Should the attacking Pokémon use moves such as Thief, Covet, Knock Off, Pluck, Bug Bite, or Incinerate, their item-stealing or item-destroying effects will resolve *before* Magician attempts to acquire the item. Similarly, Sticky Barb's self-transferring mechanism takes priority over Magician's acquisition. Activation is prevented if the Pokémon holds a Gem, even if that Gem is consumed during the move's execution. Yet, if a Power Herb is consumed from the user's possession during the move, Magician *will* proceed.

When a target's consumable item (like a Focus Sash or Lum Berry) is activated by the incoming attack, it gets used up before Magician can claim it. In contrast, items such as a Focus Band or Rocky Helmet held by the target can trigger their effects and *then* be subsequently pilfered by Magician. Should the Magician-wielding Pokémon faint mid-move (whether from the target's Liquid Ooze, a Rocky Helmet, a recoil move, or any other self-fainting effect), the Ability will fail to secure an item. Furthermore, if the attack causes Mummy to activate on the user, thereby replacing Magician, no item will be stolen.

For multi-strike attacks, Magician takes effect only after the final hit connects. Its effect still triggers even if the user is forced out via U-turn or Volt Switch, or if the target is switched out by Dragon Tail or Circle Throw. Pickpocket resolves *after* Magician; consequently, if the move is a contact move, the Pokémon with Pickpocket will ultimately acquire the item. In the specific case where Meloetta possesses Magician (through effects like Skill Swap) and uses Relic Song, the item theft occurs before its form transformation.

Items cannot be pilfered from a Pokémon with the Sticky Hold Ability, *unless* the attack itself causes that Pokémon to faint. Forbidden items for theft include Mail and Z-Crystals. Additionally, several powerful items are immune to Magician's grasp under specific circumstances: a Griseous Orb from or by Giratina, a Plate from or by Arceus, a memory from or by Silvally, a Drive from or by Genesect, a Mega Stone if either combatant can Mega Evolve with it, a Blue Orb from or by Kyogre, a Red Orb from or by Groudon, the Rusted Sword from or by Zacian, the Rusted Shield from or by Zamazenta, and Booster Energy if either Pokémon has Protosynthesis or Quark Drive.

Within the game Pokémon UNITE, Magician functions as Hoopa's unique Ability. During battles featuring distinct ally and opposing team territories, this Ability spontaneously generates a warp hole beneath a randomly selected Berry on the adversary's side, instantly transporting it directly to Hoopa. However, this power becomes inactive when Hoopa assumes its Unbound form. Notably, a befriended Hoopa Emerald is found to possess Magician as its inherent Ability. Uniquely, Hoopa is the sole Pokémon whose Magician Ability is not classified as a Hidden Ability. All Pokémon capable of having the Magician Ability originate from Generation VI.

Title: Bulletproof (Ability)

Bulletproof, an Ability known as ぼうだん (Bulletproof) in Japanese, was introduced in Generation VI. Before Generation VII, it served as the signature Ability for Chespin's evolutionary line exclusively. Pokémon possessing Bulletproof are completely immune to attacks categorized as ball or bomb moves. This immunity also prevents healing from an ally's Pollen Puff. The rationale behind the classification of several ball and bomb moves is often obscured by their English names, which differ from their Japanese equivalents. For example, Acid Spray is known as アシッドボム (Acid Bomb) in Japanese. Aura Sphere translates to はどうだん (Wave Bomb). Beak Blast carries the Japanese name くちばしキャノン (Beak Cannon). Focus Blast is termed きあいだま (Fighting Spirit Bullet). Octazooka aligns with オクタンほう (Okutank Cannon). Pollen Puff corresponds to かふんだんご (Pollen Ball). Rock Wrecker is referred to as がんせきほう (Rock Cannon). Lastly, Searing Shot's Japanese name is かえんだん (Flame Bomb). Interestingly, despite some affected moves having "cannon" in both their English and Japanese nomenclature, Spike Cannon, Flash Cannon, Hydro Cannon, Fleur Cannon, Dynamax Cannon, and Armor Cannon are not impacted by Bulletproof.

Title: Competitive (Ability)
Known in Japanese as かちき (Determined Spirit), Competitive is an Ability that made its debut in Generation VI. Should an opposing Pokémon decrease any of this Ability holder's stats, its Special Attack stat instantly rises by two stages. However, Competitive does not trigger if the Pokémon itself lowers its own stats (for example, through a move like Close Combat) or if an allied Pokémon is responsible for the stat reduction. When Special Attack itself is lowered, Competitive subsequently boosts it, leading to a net gain of one stage if initially lowered by one stage, or no net change if decreased by two stages. Given the absence of any moves that can decrease Special Attack by three stages, it is practically impossible to achieve a net reduction in a Competitive Pokémon's Special Attack without first nullifying its Ability. In instances where multiple stats are simultaneously lowered (such as through Memento or Venom Drench), Competitive activates individually for every stat affected. Its activation sequence precedes that of a held White Herb; consequently, if Competitive's effect removes all negative stat stages, the White Herb will not find an opportunity to activate. Before Generation IX, the Pokémon Piplup, Prinplup, and Empoleon possessed Defiant as their Hidden Ability, rather than Competitive.

Title: Strong Jaw (Ability)

Known in Japanese as がんじょうあご (Strong Jaw), this Ability first made its debut in Generation VI. Strong Jaw amplifies the destructive potential of the Pokémon's biting attacks by 50%. A subsequent table details the specific attacks that receive a boost from Strong Jaw, alongside the Pokémon capable of possessing this Ability and simultaneously learning those respective moves. It is also noted that Strong Jaw increases the power of the Pokémon's biting moves by 20%. Furthermore, the attack Fishious Rend sees its power enhanced by Strong Jaw, a consequence of its Japanese designation as 「エラがみ」 (Gill Bite).

Title: Refrigerate (Ability)

Known in Japanese as フリーズスキン (Freeze Skin), Refrigerate is an Ability first introduced in the sixth generation of Pokémon games. Beginning with Generation VIII, Amaura and Aurorus exclusively possess this Ability as their signature trait. When a Pokémon with Refrigerate employs a Normal-type move, that move's type is converted to Ice, and its power simultaneously increases by 30%. However, Electrify takes precedence over Refrigerate; if a Pokémon is affected by Electrify, the move will instead become Electric-type, and Refrigerate's power augmentation will not occur. The type alteration caused by Refrigerate also precedes Ion Deluge; therefore, should both effects be present, an initially Normal-type attack will ultimately manifest as an Ice-type move, since it ceases to be Normal-type prior to Ion Deluge's application. When a Pokémon with Refrigerate chooses Max Strike, the move transforms into Max Hailstorm upon execution. Should Max Strike be utilized by a Gigantamax Lapras also possessing Refrigerate, the move will instead manifest as G-Max Resonance. Specific moves that interact with Refrigerate, alongside the Pokémon capable of having this Ability and learning those moves, are typically cataloged. However, certain moves, despite being affected by Refrigerate, are currently not learnable by any Pokémon that naturally possesses the Ability. These moves can still be utilized if generated through actions like Metronome, Mirror Move, Copycat, or Mimic, or if a Pokémon acquires Refrigerate via another Ability such as Trace or Receiver, or through moves like Skill Swap or Role Play. Within the game Pokémon Rumble World, Mega Glalie exhibits the Refrigerate Ability, which similarly converts the type of Normal-type moves to Ice. In this specific title, Normal-type moves transform into Ice-type and inflict an additional 20-25% damage. Furthermore, when Nature Power is employed, while Refrigerate's activation occurs, the specific move subsequently selected by Nature Power does not undergo the Ice-type conversion, nor does it receive any power enhancement.

Title: Sweet Veil (Ability)

Debuting in Generation VI, Sweet Veil (スイートベール Sweet Veil in Japanese) is an Ability that, before Generation VII, was exclusive to Swirlix and Slurpuff. Any Pokémon with Sweet Veil, alongside its entire team (including non-adjacent allies), gains immunity to the sleep status condition. As a result, the move Rest will not succeed if used by the Ability's possessor or any of its allies, unless the Rest user itself has an Ability that disregards others. Additionally, if Yawn is targeted at the Sweet Veil user or its allies (even non-adjacent ones), the move will fail. It further ensures that Pokémon already made drowsy by Yawn on the Sweet Veil user's side will not transition into sleep.

Title: Stance Change (Ability)

Known in Japanese as バトルスイッチ (Battle Switch), Stance Change is an Ability that made its debut in Generation VI. This unique Ability is exclusive to Aegislash. Through Stance Change, Aegislash dynamically shifts between its Shield Forme and Blade Forme. When not engaged in combat, Aegislash maintains its Shield Forme, and consequently, withdrawing from battle will cause it to revert to this defensive posture. Should Aegislash, while in Shield Forme, employ a damaging attack, it will transition into Blade Forme an instant prior to executing the move. Conversely, if Aegislash is in Blade Forme and utilizes King's Shield, it will transform back into Shield Forme just before the move's activation. Form changes are not triggered by status moves, with the sole exception of King's Shield. Furthermore, moves that invoke other moves, such as Sleep Talk, will not induce a form alteration, even if the invoked move is a damaging one or King's Shield. The moves Gastro Acid, Worry Seed, and Simple Beam will fail when targeting a Pokémon with Stance Change. Similarly, Role Play, Skill Swap, Entrainment, and Doodle cannot be successfully used if either participant possesses Stance Change. Abilities such as Trace, Power of Alchemy, or Receiver are unable to copy Stance Change. This Ability resists being replaced by Mummy or Lingering Aroma, suppressed by Core Enforcer or Neutralizing Gas, or exchanged via Wandering Spirit. Should a Pokémon other than Aegislash acquire Stance Change through Imposter or Transform, that Pokémon will not exhibit form changes. Should Aegislash *attempt* a move, even if its execution is prevented by an effect such as a status condition, confusion, or disobedience, Stance Change will nonetheless activate as usual. However, if Aegislash attempts a move but cannot execute it because of a status condition or confusion, Stance Change will not activate. Within Pokémon Legends: Z-A, the concept of Abilities is absent from standard gameplay. Nevertheless, Aegislash retains its form-changing mechanism between Shield and Blade Formes, adhering to the same conditions found in prior game installments. Because of Z-A's real-time combat system, Aegislash remains vulnerable to attacks during its form change animation. Its form is not officially considered altered until the completion of this animation. The core function of Stance Change is to enable Aegislash to alternate between its Shield Forme and Blade Forme. When Aegislash, in Shield Forme, initiates a damaging attack, it shifts into Blade Forme right before the move is executed. Conversely, an Aegislash in Blade Forme will revert to Shield Forme directly preceding its use of King's Shield. Upon entering a new floor, Aegislash will adopt its Shield Forme. Furthermore, this Ability cannot be modified or sealed. In the context of Pokémon UNITE, Stance Change functions as Aegislash's signature Ability. It empowers the user to transition between Blade Forme and Shield Forme. Executing a blade move causes the user to adopt Blade Forme, resulting in boosted movement speed, Attack, and basic attack speed. Conversely, utilizing a shield move converts the user to Shield Forme, enhancing its Defense and Special Defense. Immediately following a transition from Shield Forme to Blade Forme, the Pokémon receives an additional, temporary increase to its movement speed and basic attack speed.

Title: Gale Wings (Ability)

Known in Japanese as はやてのつばさ (Gale Wings), this Ability made its debut in Generation VI. It is an exclusive characteristic of the Fletchling evolutionary lineage. Gale Wings grants a one-stage boost to the priority of Flying-type techniques. Such accelerated Flying-type offensive and status moves are susceptible to being intercepted by Quick Guard. However, this Ability fails to enhance the priority of Flying-type Hidden Power, Natural Gift, or Judgment, as these specific moves are categorized as Normal-type before their execution. In its current iteration, Gale Wings activates only if the user possesses full HP when the move is selected. It also provides no priority increase to Flying-type Tera Blast. Within the Pokémon UNITE game, Talonflame possesses Gale Wings as its Ability, which elevates the user's movement speed by 10% when their HP is at 85% or higher.

Title: Mega Launcher (Ability)

Known in Japan as メガランチャー Mega Launcher, this Ability first appeared in Generation VI. Beginning with Generation VIII, Clauncher and its evolution, Clawitzer, possess Mega Launcher as their exclusive trait. When a Pokémon has Mega Launcher, the potency of its aura and pulse attacks is enhanced. Offensive moves see their power amplified by half (50%), and the recovery effect of Heal Pulse, including Z-Heal Pulse, restores three-quarters (75%) of the target's total HP, surpassing its standard 50%. A comprehensive list of moves impacted by Mega Launcher, alongside the Pokémon capable of both possessing the Ability and learning those specific moves, is provided in the accompanying table. Despite being influenced by Mega Launcher, a set of moves listed subsequently cannot be naturally acquired by any Pokémon possessing this Ability at present. Nonetheless, these moves can still be utilized with Mega Launcher's benefit if invoked through mechanisms like Metronome, Copycat, or Mimic. Alternatively, a Pokémon might gain Mega Launcher via Abilities such as Trace or Receiver, or moves like Skill Swap or Role Play, enabling them to use these otherwise unlearnable attacks with the boost. This Ability also strengthens aura and pulse moves used by a Pokémon with it, where damage-dealing attacks receive a 20% power increase, and Heal Pulse restores 48% of the target's maximum HP instead of the typical 40%. The Ability's effect targets moves whose Japanese names incorporate the term はどう hadō, which translates to either 'wave' or 'aura'.

Title: Grass Pelt (Ability)

Known in Japanese as くさのけがわ (Grass Pelt), this Ability was introduced during Generation VI. It uniquely serves as the signature Ability for the Pokémon Skiddo and Gogoat. Its primary effect dictates that while Grassy Terrain is active, the Defense stat of the Pokémon possessing this Ability experiences a 50% increase. This defensive boost, however, does not apply to damage sustained from self-inflicted confusion. Furthermore, a functionally similar effect exists in Pokémon Conquest, named "Grass Cloak" (はっぱのころも Leaf Cloak), which likewise grants a boost to the user's Defense stat when they are positioned on a grass tile.

Title: Symbiosis (Ability)

Known in Japanese as きょうせい, Symbiosis is an Ability first seen in Generation VI. Before Generation VII, it served as a unique Ability for the Flabébé evolution family. By Generation VIII, Oranguru held the distinction of having Symbiosis as its exclusive Ability. When a Pokémon possessing Symbiosis holds an item, it will transfer that item to an ally right after the ally's held item is used up. In Triple Battles, Symbiosis can even provide an item to an ally not positioned directly next to the user.

The Ability activates whenever an allied Pokémon expends its item, irrespective of whether it's used directly or via moves like Fling or Natural Gift. Should a Pokémon consume another's Berry using Bug Bite or Pluck while not holding an item itself, Symbiosis from an ally will be prompted, bestowing an item upon the Pokémon that performed the move. The bursting of an Air Balloon also initiates Symbiosis. In scenarios like Triple Battles or Horde Encounters where multiple Pokémon on one side have Symbiosis, the Ability will activate for the Pokémon with the higher speed stat, even when under the influence of Trick Room.

However, Symbiosis remains dormant if an ally's item is transferred to another Pokémon (e.g., by Thief or even Symbiosis itself), obliterated by Incinerate, or dislodged by Knock Off. When a damage-reducing Berry is eaten in response to an assault, Symbiosis's activation is delayed until after the damage calculation is complete. Similarly, if an item is consumed through Fling or Natural Gift, Symbiosis will not take effect until the move has dealt its damage.

Certain items are immune to Symbiosis's transfer effect: Z-Crystals are untransferable. Furthermore, specific exclusive items cannot be passed if either the Symbiosis user or the recipient is the designated Pokémon: this includes a Griseous Orb for Giratina, a Plate for Arceus, a memory for Silvally, a Drive for Genesect, a Mega Stone if a Pokémon can Mega Evolve with it, a Blue Orb for Kyogre, a Red Orb for Groudon, a Booster Energy for a Paradox Pokémon (excluding Koraidon, Miraidon, Gouging Fire, Raging Bolt, Iron Boulder, and Iron Crown), or a Mask (Cornerstone Mask, Hearthflame Mask, or Wellspring Mask) for Ogerpon.

Should an ally of a Symbiosis user consume a Gem via a move, Symbiosis is triggered right away. If the transferred item would typically modify the power of the activating move, its effect is applied instantly; similarly, if a consumable item (excluding another Gem) is received and can be used, it will be activated without delay. Nonetheless, if a Plate or Drive is provided to a Pokémon performing Judgment or Techno Blast after it has already used a Gem, the move's type will remain unaltered. Correspondingly, if a Pokémon gains an additional Gem through Symbiosis after consuming a Gem, it will not consume the newly acquired Gem as well.

Exclusively in Generation VI, when an ally's Eject Button is consumed, Symbiosis will engage, passing an item to that ally after it departs the field but prior to its substitute entering. Upon the return of this Pokémon to battle, its item will be subject to the Symbiosis Eject Button glitch, a phenomenon that leads specific items to trigger their effects twice. Conversely, if an ally of a Symbiosis holder uses a move to consume a Gem, Symbiosis will only become active after the execution of that move. It is important to note that the simple activation of an Eject Button does not cause Symbiosis to trigger.

Title: Tough Claws (Ability)

An Ability known as Tough Claws (Japanese: かたいツメ Tough Claws) made its debut in Generation VI. It enhances the strength of a Pokémon's contact attacks by roughly 30%, or more accurately, by a factor of 5325/4096. A provided table generally outlines moves impacted by Tough Claws, along with Pokémon capable of having the Ability and learning these moves. However, certain moves, despite being affected by this Ability, are presently not acquirable by any Pokémon that naturally possesses Tough Claws. Nevertheless, their usage becomes possible if a Pokémon with Tough Claws acquires the move through Mimic, or if a Pokémon gains Tough Claws itself via abilities such as Trace or Receiver, or through moves like Skill Swap or Role Play. Separately, Tough Claws is also stated to increase the damage output of contact maneuvers by 20%. It was documented in the PokéSPedia data-book that X's Charizard, named Salamè, possesses Tough Claws as its Ability upon Mega Evolving into Mega Charizard X. This Ability is present on three distinct Mega-Evolved Pokémon, thereby matching Magic Bounce as the most frequently occurring Ability among all Mega-Evolved forms.

Title: Pixilate (Ability)

Pixilate (Japanese: フェアリースキン Fairy Skin) is an Ability that made its debut in Generation VI. Since Generation VIII, it has been recognized as the exclusive Ability of Sylveon. This Ability transforms all Normal-type attacks executed by the Pokémon into Fairy-type moves, simultaneously granting them a 30% increase in power. The effect of Electrify takes precedence over Pixilate; therefore, if the Pokémon is under the influence of Electrify, the move will become Electric-type and will not receive Pixilate's power amplification. Conversely, Pixilate's type-changing mechanism activates before Ion Deluge. This means that if both effects are in play, an attack that originated as Normal-type will ultimately be a Fairy-type move, as its typing would have already changed by the time Ion Deluge would apply. When Max Strike is chosen by a Pokémon with Pixilate, it will manifest as Max Starfall upon use, with the sole exception of Gigantamax Alcremie, whose Max Strike will instead convert into G-Max Finale. The following table identifies the specific moves impacted by Pixilate, alongside the Pokémon capable of possessing Pixilate and learning those particular moves. While some moves are indeed affected by this Ability, no Pokémon currently possessing Pixilate can natively learn them. Nonetheless, these moves can still be utilized if called by Metronome, Mirror Move, Copycat, or Mimic, or if a Pokémon temporarily gains Pixilate via an Ability such as Trace or Receiver, or a move like Skill Swap or Role Play. In Pokémon Rumble World, both Mega Gardevoir and Altaria are endowed with the Pixilate ability, converting Normal-type attacks into Fairy-type and causing them to inflict 20-25% more damage. Within Pokémon UNITE, Pixilate serves as Sylveon's unique Ability. It provides a 2.5% boost to the user's Special Attack and Special Defense for 1.5 seconds each time it deals or receives damage, with this beneficial effect accumulating up to 6 times.

Title: Aerilate (Ability)

Originating in Generation VI, Aerilate (known in Japanese as スカイスキン Sky Skin) is an ability. When a Pokémon with Aerilate uses a Normal-type move, that move's type transforms into Flying, simultaneously gaining a 30% increase in power. Electrify's effect takes precedence over Aerilate; thus, if the Pokémon is under the influence of Electrify, the move will become Electric-type, and Aerilate's power augmentation will not occur. Conversely, Aerilate's type modification occurs prior to Ion Deluge. Consequently, if both effects are active, an initially Normal-type move will ultimately resolve as Flying-type, given that it ceases to be Normal-type by the time Ion Deluge's effect would apply. Information regarding moves influenced by Aerilate, along with the Pokémon capable of possessing this ability and learning those moves, is typically presented in a subsequent table. Certain moves are indeed impacted by this Ability, yet no Pokémon naturally possessing Aerilate can learn them at present. Nevertheless, these moves can still be executed if chosen through actions like Metronome, Mirror Move, Copycat, or Mimic. Alternatively, a Pokémon that acquired Aerilate via another ability (e.g., Trace, Receiver) or a move (e.g., Skill Swap, Role Play) could utilize them. Within Pokémon Rumble World, Mega Pinsir and Salamence exhibit the Aerilate ability, which converts their Normal-type attacks into Flying-type. Furthermore, these now Flying-type moves inflict 20-25% additional damage. Notably, Aerilate stands alone as the sole Ability exclusive to Mega-Evolved Pokémon that is not classified as a signature ability.

Title: Parental Bond (Ability)

Parental Bond (known in Japanese as おやこあい, or Parent-Child Love) is an Ability introduced in Generation VI. It is exclusive to Mega Kangaskhan. This Ability causes most damaging attacks performed by the Pokémon to become two-strike moves. However, it does not apply to moves that inherently strike multiple times.

A move that has the potential to hit multiple targets (including allies), such as Earthquake or Rock Slide, will not strike a second time. Nevertheless, if the move can only hit a single Pokémon—either because it's a Single Battle, or a multi-target move is used when only one valid target is present—it will then strike twice. Should a move capable of hitting multiple Pokémon only connect with one due to others missing, it will register only a single strike.

Because Parental Bond converts moves into two-hit multi-strike attacks, each strike has its own independent chance to land a critical hit. Items and Abilities that activate upon a strike or contact, such as Cursed Body and Rocky Helmet, will trigger for each individual strike. Conversely, protective moves like Spiky Shield and King's Shield will inflict damage or decrease Attack (respectively) only once if they guard against a contact move from a Parental Bond user. Furthermore, there is a single accuracy check for the entire attack, meaning both strikes either hit or both miss.

Any offensive move possessing a secondary effect (with the exception of Secret Power) will apply that same secondary effect on both strikes (e.g., Power-Up Punch). If a secondary effect has a percentage chance of activation, each strike has an independent chance to trigger it. Even if the Pokémon's Ability is altered to Mummy after the initial strike, the second strike will still occur. Pay Day releases coins only after the first strike. Incinerate, however, destroys applicable held items after each strike.

In contrast to other secondary effects, Secret Power's secondary effect can only activate following the final strike. If a move inflicts recoil damage, the recoil amount is calculated based on the total damage dealt by both strikes, but it is applied after the final strike. Struggle, specifically, will inflict recoil damage equivalent to half the user's maximum HP after the last strike. Moves that compel the target to switch out or those that force the user to switch out will strike twice, then trigger the forced switch after both strikes are completed. Thief, Covet, Bug Bite, and Pluck do not steal or consume the target's held item until the final strike has occurred; therefore, if the target could use its item after the first strike (e.g., due to low HP), it will do so before the attacker can take it. Similarly, Smelling Salts, Wake-Up Slap, and Knock Off do not cure the target's status condition or remove its held item (respectively) until after the final strike, ensuring both strikes benefit from the increased power. Fire-type moves, Scald, and Steam Eruption will thaw a frozen target after the final strike (preventing a frozen target from being thawed and subsequently burned by the same move). Smack Down and Thousand Arrows will only ground the target after the final strike. If Meloetta has Parental Bond and uses Relic Song, it will change Forme only once, after the second strike. Burn Up does not remove the user's Fire type until after the second strike, ensuring both strikes receive the same-type attack bonus.

When a Pokémon with Parental Bond uses an Electric-type move against a Pokémon with Lightning Rod, or a Water-type move against a Pokémon with Storm Drain, the Special Attack boost received by the target will only occur once. If Present heals the target, it will perform only a single strike, but if it inflicts damage, it will strike twice (with the second strike guaranteed to damage the target). Fixed-damage moves (such as Seismic Toss and Dragon Rage) will deal their full specified damage on both strikes. The damage output of Psywave is determined independently for each strike, and the second strike's damage is not reduced. Each strike of Super Fang halves the target's HP (effectively reducing it to a quarter if no HP changes occur between strikes). Counter, Mirror Coat, Metal Burst, and Bide will deal their full calculated damage for both strikes. The initial strike of Assurance counts as the target having previously taken damage, thus boosting the power of the second strike. Fury Cutter and Echoed Voice only account for uses of the move rather than individual hits, so the second strike's power is not amplified by the first. Grass Pledge, Fire Pledge, and Water Pledge will strike twice, even when used as part of a combination move. Natural Gift and Spit Up also strike twice.

Moves that necessitate a recharge turn after use will strike twice, but the user only needs to recharge for a single turn. One-hit knockout moves, Fling, Self-Destruct, Explosion, Final Gambit, Uproar, Rollout, and Ice Ball will only strike once. (Other consecutively executed moves, such as Outrage, are capable of striking twice.) Moves that involve a charging turn (e.g., Fly and Solar Beam) will only strike once, even if the Pokémon achieves a fully charged state in one turn (such as by holding a Power Herb). Endeavor also performs only one strike, even if the user or target's HP is modified after it strikes (e.g., by Iron Barbs or a Sitrus Berry). Confusion damage occurs only once. Spirit Shackle and Anchor Shot will only trap the target after the final strike.

The second strike, initially dealing 50% of its usual damage, was later adjusted to deal 25% of its usual damage (unless it is a fixed-damage move). Parental Bond has no effect on Z-Moves or Max Moves.

In Pokémon Super Mystery Dungeon, when Kangaskhan Mega Evolves using the Awakening Emera, Parental Bond instead causes a baby Kangaskhan to join the party. This baby Kangaskhan functions similarly to client Pokémon, acting independently and beyond player control. It disregards team tactics and consistently follows its mother. It shares its mother's moveset, possesses approximately one-third of her power, and spawns with 100 HP. Once the Awakening Emera's effect expires, the baby Kangaskhan enters Berserk mode alongside its mother, though it will warp back to its mother if it strays too far. When the Berserk mode concludes, the baby Kangaskhan vanishes.

Title: Dark Aura (Ability)

Debuting in Generation VI, Dark Aura (Japanese: ダークオーラ Dark Aura) is an Ability uniquely associated with Yveltal as its signature power. For all Pokémon on the field, it significantly amplifies the potency of Dark-type attacks by an approximate 33%, or more precisely, by a factor of 5448/4096. This amplification is entirely negated by Aura Break, which instead causes Dark-type attacks to have their power divided by 4/3, manifesting as a 25% decrease in damage output. Importantly, the benefits of Dark Aura do not accumulate if multiple Pokémon possess this Ability simultaneously. Furthermore, on a given floor, Dark Aura enhances the strength of Dark-type moves for every Pokémon present by around 40-45%. This particular boosting effect is also counteracted by Aura Break.

Title: Fairy Aura (Ability)

Fairy Aura, known as フェアリーオーラ in Japanese, made its debut as an Ability in Generation VI. It uniquely serves as the signature Ability for Xerneas. Across the battlefield, this Ability boosts the efficacy of Fairy-type attacks for all participating Pokémon. This enhancement is roughly 33% (or, with greater precision, by a multiplier of 5448/4096). However, Aura Break entirely reverses this impact, instead causing Fairy-type attack power to be diminished by a factor of 4/3, which results in a 25% decrease in overall damage. It is important to note that the effects of Fairy Aura do not accumulate even if multiple Pokémon possess the Ability. In certain gameplay environments, Fairy Aura also delivers an approximate 40-45% power increase to Fairy-type moves used by all Pokémon sharing the same floor. Aura Break likewise nullifies this particular enhancement. Finally, within the X & Y arc's Japan Mini-volume 6, it was disclosed that Xerxer, Y's Xerneas, possesses Fairy Aura as its designated Ability.

Title: Aura Break (Ability)

First appearing in Generation VI, Aura Break (Japanese: オーラブレイク Aura Break) serves as one of Zygarde's signature Abilities. This power fundamentally reverses the usual impact of Fairy Aura and Dark Aura. Instead of those Abilities multiplying the power of Fairy- or Dark-type moves by their typical factor of approximately 4/3 (or, more precisely, 5448/4096), Aura Break causes such moves to have their power divided by 4/3, leading to a 25% reduction in damage output while both Aura Abilities remain active. Even when a Pokémon wielding Mold Breaker, Teravolt, or Turboblaze executes a Fairy- or Dark-type move, the effect of Aura Break still applies.

In Generation VII, a Zygarde equipped with Aura Break can be dismantled back into Cores and Cells by utilizing the Reassembly Unit. Exclusively in Generation VIII, the Zygarde Cube provides the means to switch Zygarde's Ability between Aura Break and Power Construct. However, across all game titles, Zygarde cannot change its Ability using either an Ability Capsule or an Ability Patch. Within Pokémon Super Mystery Dungeon, this Ability proves practically ineffective. Its lack of utility stems from Zygarde not being encountered as an enemy, the inability to battle Xerneas or Yveltal while controlling Zygarde, and the impossibility of including Zygarde on the same team as Xerneas or Yveltal, unless one is summoned through a Djinn's Bottle.

Title: Primordial Sea (Ability)

Known in Japanese as はじまりのうみ (Sea of the Beginning), Primordial Sea is an Ability that made its debut in Generation VI, specifically in Pokémon Omega Ruby and Alpha Sapphire. It is the signature Ability exclusively belonging to Primal Kyogre. This Ability generates heavy rain, a unique variant of standard rain, when a Pokémon possessing Primordial Sea enters the battle or when a Pokémon gains this Ability. In the specific context of a Rotation Battle, Primordial Sea will not activate if its user is sent out into a rotated-out position, nor will it take effect when that Pokémon is subsequently rotated in. Furthermore, the Ability's activation is prevented if heavy rain is already established on the battlefield. Beyond the typical effects of rain, heavy rain uniquely causes damage-dealing Fire-type moves to fail outright, unless a Pokémon on the field has either the Air Lock or Cloud Nine Ability. Additionally, this severe weather condition causes the weather-modifying moves Sunny Day, Rain Dance, Sandstorm, and Hail to fail if they are attempted, and prevents the Abilities Drought, Drizzle, Sand Stream, and Snow Warning from activating. Once in effect, the heavy rain persists as long as any Pokémon with the active Primordial Sea Ability remains on the field (even if it was not the Pokémon that initially created the weather), unless it is replaced by another weather condition. If the sole Pokémon on the field with Primordial Sea is switched out, rotated out, or has its Ability suppressed or replaced, the heavy rain will dissipate. Heavy rain can be superseded by the effects of Desolate Land or Delta Stream. It's also noteworthy that rain generated by Primordial Sea does not allow Sliggoo to evolve into Goodra. In Pokémon Rumble World, Primal Kyogre's Primordial Sea Ability grants it complete immunity to Fire-type moves.

Title: Desolate Land (Ability)

Bearing the Japanese name おわりのだいち (Land of the End), Desolate Land is an Ability that made its debut in Generation VI, specifically within Pokémon Omega Ruby and Alpha Sapphire. It serves as the unique signature Ability of Primal Groudon. Upon a Pokémon possessing Desolate Land entering the fray, or if a Pokémon acquires this Ability, it immediately conjures extremely harsh sunlight. This is a distinct and potent form of harsh sunlight. In the context of a Rotation Battle, Desolate Land will not take effect if its bearer is deployed in a rotated-out slot, nor will it activate when rotated into play. Furthermore, the Ability remains dormant if extremely harsh sunlight already blankets the battlefield. Beyond the standard consequences of harsh sunlight, this intensified weather condition renders damage-dealing Water-type moves ineffective. An exception occurs if a Pokémon on the field possesses either the Air Lock or Cloud Nine Ability. Moreover, extremely harsh sunlight prevents the activation of weather-modifying Abilities such as Drought, Drizzle, Sand Stream, and Snow Warning, and causes the moves Sunny Day, Rain Dance, Sandstorm, and Hail to fail when attempted. Once established, this extremely harsh sunlight persists as long as any Pokémon with an active Desolate Land Ability remains on the field, regardless of which Pokémon initially summoned it, unless it is superseded. The weather effect will cease, however, if the sole Pokémon with Desolate Land is rotated out, switched out, or has its Ability suppressed or replaced. Its powerful effects can only be overturned by the Abilities Primordial Sea or Delta Stream. Although Abilities are absent from standard gameplay in Pokémon Legends: Z-A, during the second phase of the Rogue Mega Evolution encounter with Primal Groudon, the creature gains immunity to Water-type attacks. Stunning Primal Groudon will temporarily lift this immunity. In Pokémon Rumble World, Primal Groudon is endowed with the Desolate Land ability, bestowing upon it complete invulnerability to Water-type moves.

Title: Delta Stream (Ability)

Delta Stream (Japanese: デルタストリーム Delta Stream) is an Ability that made its debut in Generation VI, specifically in Pokémon Omega Ruby and Alpha Sapphire. It serves as Mega Rayquaza's exclusive Ability. When a Pokémon with Delta Stream enters a battle, or when a Pokémon gains this Ability, a distinct atmospheric condition known as strong winds is generated.

In the specific scenario of a Rotation Battle, Delta Stream will not activate if the Pokémon is brought out in a rotated-out position, nor will its effect manifest when that Pokémon is subsequently rotated into an active position. Additionally, Delta Stream's activation is prevented if strong winds are already active on the battlefield, or if the Pokémon's Ability is suppressed prior to it acquiring Delta Stream.

Strong winds cause moves that would normally be super effective against a pure Flying-type Pokémon to instead deal neutral damage, effectively negating the Flying type's usual weaknesses. This effect does not apply if a Pokémon with Cloud Nine or Air Lock is present on the field. Outside of Inverse Battles, this modification means that Electric-, Ice-, and Rock-type attacks will inflict normal damage on Flying-type Pokémon. During Inverse Battles, however, this results in Bug-, Fighting-, Grass-, and Ground-type moves dealing neutral damage to Flying-type Pokémon. For dual-typed Pokémon, if a move is no longer super effective against the Flying type and is not super effective against its other type, the hit is no longer considered supereffective for purposes such as damage-reducing Berries.

The presence of strong winds has no impact on the mechanics of Stealth Rock or Anticipation. Furthermore, these potent winds cause the weather-modifying moves Sunny Day, Rain Dance, Sandstorm, and Hail to fail if attempted, and similarly prevent the Abilities Drought, Drizzle, Sand Stream, and Snow Warning from activating. Nevertheless, strong winds can be replaced by the effects of Desolate Land or Primordial Sea.

Once strong winds are established, they will persist as long as any active Pokémon on the field possesses Delta Stream as its Ability (even if it wasn't the Pokémon that initially created them), unless Delta Stream itself is suppressed or replaced. The strong winds will dissipate if the sole Pokémon on the field with Delta Stream is rotated out, switched out, or has its Ability suppressed or replaced.

In the game Pokémon Rumble World, Mega Rayquaza is depicted with the Delta Stream ability, which removes the weaknesses inherent to its Flying typing, defensively rendering it akin to a pure Dragon-type. Rayquaza acquires the Delta Stream Ability upon undergoing Mega Evolution. Delta Stream holds the distinction of being the last Generation VI Ability in index number order.

Title: Stamina (Ability)

This entry focuses on the Ability named Stamina; for other uses of the term, please see Stamina (disambiguation). Known as じきゅうりょく (Stamina) in Japanese, this Ability made its debut in Generation VII. Prior to Generation IX, it was exclusively the signature Ability of Mudbray and Mudsdale. Upon being struck by an opposing attack, a Pokémon benefiting from Stamina will see its Defense stat increase by a single stage. Should a Pokémon featuring this Ability be targeted by a multi-hit technique (such as Fury Swipes), the effect of Stamina triggers for every individual strike. Any accompanying statistics are given as exact figures, not mere base stats, and are custom-configured rather than being determined by calculations involving base stats, level, Nature, Individual Values (IVs), and Effort Values (EVs). In terms of index numbering, Stamina holds the distinction of being the inaugural Ability introduced in Generation VII.

Title: Wimp Out (Ability)

Debuting in Generation VII, Wimp Out (Japanese: にげごし Back Off) is an Ability exclusively possessed by Wimpod as its signature trait. Should a Pokémon with Wimp Out sustain damage that reduces its HP below half of its maximum, it will either flee in a wild encounter or automatically switch out during a Trainer battle. This Ability remains inactive if the Pokémon's HP is already less than half, unless its HP is first restored. While Wimp Out does not trigger if the Pokémon's HP drops below half from self-inflicted damage due to confusion, it *will* activate from all other damage sources causing HP to fall below half, including Struggle recoil. Activation does not occur if the Pokémon's HP is lowered by means other than direct damage, such as Pain Split, or self-inflicted reductions from moves like Substitute, Belly Drum, or Curse. Furthermore, Wimp Out will not activate if a move modified by Sheer Force reduces the Pokémon's HP below half. For multistrike moves, the Ability's activation is deferred until after the final hit, even if the Wimp Out-bearing Pokémon's HP drops below half at an earlier strike. If this Ability is triggered by an attack like U-turn or Volt Switch, the Pokémon employing that move will not be forced to switch out. The Ability will not activate if the Pokémon's HP falls below half while it is suspended in the air during the semi-invulnerable turn of Sky Drop. When the Pokémon's HP drops below half and a Berry (e.g., a Sitrus Berry) immediately restores it above half, Wimp Out will not trigger; however, if HP drops below half and then recovers above half via a Shell Bell, Wimp Out *will* activate even after the Shell Bell's restorative effect. Trapping moves do not impede Wimp Out's activation. In Trainer battles, Wimp Out will fail to activate if the Pokémon possessing the Ability is its Trainer's only remaining Pokémon. It also will not activate on the player's Pokémon in wild battles during trials. Should the Pokémon carrying Wimp Out also hold a Red Card or Eject Button, the held item's effect takes precedence. Moves such as Dragon Tail and Circle Throw cause the Pokémon to switch out prior to Wimp Out's activation. Wimp Out stands as one of only four signature Abilities, alongside Honey Gather, Battery, and Ball Fetch, that were exclusively granted to a pre-evolved Pokémon upon their introduction.

Title: Emergency Exit (Ability)

Introduced in Generation VII, Emergency Exit (ききかいひ Crisis Prevention in Japanese) is an Ability. Golisopod possesses this unique Ability as its signature trait. When a Pokémon with Emergency Exit sustains damage that lowers its Hit Points (HP) below half of its maximum, it will automatically flee from wild encounters or switch out during Trainer battles. This Ability will not trigger if the Pokémon's HP is already under the halfway mark, unless its HP is first recovered.

If a Pokémon's HP drops below half due to self-inflicted damage from confusion, Emergency Exit will not activate; however, it *will* activate for all other forms of damage, including recoil from Struggle. Its activation is also prevented if HP is lowered by means other than damage, such as Pain Split, or self-inflicted HP reduction from moves like Substitute, Belly Drum, or Curse. Emergency Exit will likewise not activate if HP falls below half from a move affected by Sheer Force.

For multi-strike moves, this Ability activates solely after the final hit, even if the Pokémon's HP drops below half before that last strike. Should Emergency Exit activate after being struck by U-turn or Volt Switch, the attacking Pokémon using those moves will not be switched out. The Ability will also not activate if the Pokémon's HP drops below half while it is airborne during the semi-invulnerable turn of Sky Drop.

If a Pokémon's HP falls below half and it immediately consumes a Berry (e.g., a Sitrus Berry) to restore its HP above half, Emergency Exit does not activate. Conversely, if HP drops below half and then recovers back above half due to a Shell Bell, Emergency Exit *will* activate after the Shell Bell's healing effect. Trapping moves do not prevent Emergency Exit from activating.

In Trainer battles, Emergency Exit will not activate if the Pokémon with this Ability is its Trainer's only remaining combatant. Player-controlled Pokémon in wild battles during trials are unable to activate Emergency Exit. If the Pokémon possessing Emergency Exit is holding a Red Card or an Eject Button, the item's effect takes precedence. Moves such as Dragon Tail and Circle Throw will switch out the Pokémon before Emergency Exit has a chance to activate.

Title: Merciless (Ability)

Merciless, an Ability first appearing in Generation VII, bears the Japanese designation ひとでなし, meaning 'Brute'. This Ability is the exclusive signature trait of Mareanie and Toxapex. Should a Pokémon wielding Merciless deliver an attack to a target afflicted with poison, that strike is guaranteed to land as a critical hit; this guarantee, however, is nullified if the target possesses Battle Armor or Shell Armor, or is under the influence of Lucky Chant. Notably, the PokéSPedia data-book confirmed that Moon's Mareanie utilizes Merciless as her Ability. A notable pun on the word ひとで (starfish) is embedded within the Ability's Japanese name, ひとでなし, offering insight into its exclusive allocation to Mareanie and Toxapex.

Title: Shields Down (Ability)

An Ability introduced in Generation VII, Shields Down is known in Japanese as リミットシールド (Limit Shield). Minior is the sole Pokémon to possess this signature Ability. Upon the commencement of a battle, or at the close of any turn, Minior transforms into its Meteor Form if its HP remains above half. Conversely, should its HP drop below half by the end of a turn, it reverts to its core form. While in Meteor Form, Minior gains immunity to non-volatile status conditions and cannot be made drowsy by Yawn. Furthermore, Minior's use of the move Rest will invariably fail while it is in its Meteor Form. When Minior is sent out in its core form and is grounded (e.g., holding Iron Ball, under Gravity, or having Ingrain passed by Baton Pass), Toxic Spikes will poison it prior to Shields Down activating its change to Meteor Form. A status condition acquired by Minior in its core form will not be cured upon its subsequent change to Meteor Form.

Certain moves, specifically Gastro Acid, Worry Seed, and Simple Beam, will be ineffective against a Pokémon possessing Shields Down. Moves like Role Play, Skill Swap, Entrainment, and Doodle cannot be successfully used if either the user or the target Pokémon has Shields Down. Shields Down is impervious to being copied by Abilities like Trace, Power of Alchemy, or Receiver. It resists replacement by Mummy or Lingering Aroma, suppression by Core Enforcer or Neutralizing Gas, and transference via Wandering Spirit. Should a Pokémon other than Minior acquire Shields Down through abilities like Imposter or Transform, it will not gain the form-changing mechanic nor the immunity to status conditions, even if it specifically transformed into a Meteor Form Minior. Abilities such as Mold Breaker, Turboblaze, and Teravolt exert no influence over Shields Down's functionality. When a Pokémon possessing Poison Touch strikes a Meteor Form Minior with Sunsteel Strike or any of its variations, the Minior will not become poisoned. Outside of combat, Minior consistently maintains its core form.

Title: Water Bubble (Ability)

This passive skill, known in Japanese as すいほう, was introduced in the Pokémon series' seventh generation. It stands as the exclusive Ability of both Dewpider and its evolved form, Araquanid. A Pokémon with Water Bubble experiences a 50% reduction in damage taken from Fire-type attacks, while simultaneously seeing the power of its own Water-type moves doubled. Moreover, this Ability grants complete immunity to the burn status condition. If a Pokémon somehow becomes burned while in battle despite having Water Bubble (such as by acquiring the Ability through an effect like Skill Swap, or being burned by an opponent with an Ability like Mold Breaker), the burn will be instantly cured.

Title: Berserk (Ability)

Introduced in Generation VII, Berserk (Japanese: ぎゃくじょう Frenzy) is an Ability. Prior to Generation VIII, it was the signature trait of Drampa. In Generation IX, Galarian Moltres possesses Berserk as its signature Ability. Each time a Pokémon with Berserk has its HP reduced below half by a direct, damaging move, its Special Attack stat is boosted by one stage. Even if a Pokémon's HP drops below the halfway point and is immediately set to be restored above half by a held item, such as a Sitrus Berry, Berserk will still trigger before the HP restoration occurs. Nevertheless, when struck by a multistrike move, the held item is consumed right after the hit that initially lowers HP below half. Therefore, Berserk will only activate if the Pokémon's HP remains below half after *all* strikes of the move have finished and *after* the held item's effect has concluded. Berserk will not activate if the HP falls below half due to indirect damage sources, including effects like Leech Seed, various status conditions, or weather phenomena. Furthermore, Berserk fails to activate if the Pokémon's HP is lowered below half by a move influenced by the Sheer Force Ability.

Title: Long Reach (Ability)

Long Reach, known as えんかく (Distant) in Japanese, debuted as an Ability in the seventh Pokémon generation. It functions as the exclusive Ability for Rowlet and its entire evolutionary line, with the sole exception of Hisuian Decidueye. When a Pokémon wielding Long Reach executes a move that ordinarily requires physical contact, it avoids triggering any effects typically caused by that contact. While a relevant table outlines the contact moves learnable by Pokémon possessing Long Reach, other contact moves are also influenced by this Ability; however, these cannot be natively learned by any Pokémon with Long Reach. Such moves can still be utilized via actions like Metronome, Mirror Move, Copycat, or Mimic. Furthermore, a Pokémon might acquire Long Reach through Abilities such as Trace or Receiver, or via moves like Skill Swap or Role Play, allowing them to use any contact move under its effect. In Pokémon Legends: Arceus's internal coding, Hisuian Decidueye's Hidden Ability is specified as Long Reach instead of Scrappy. For Pokémon UNITE, Long Reach is Decidueye's designated Ability, which provides a 20% boost to damage inflicted upon distant opponents. This bonus specifically excludes any supplemental damage added per level from a move's inherent damage formula.

Title: Liquid Voice (Ability)

An Ability first appearing in Generation VII, Liquid Voice (Japanese: うるおいボイス, meaning Moist Voice) is a distinctive capability. It is a signature characteristic of Popplio's evolutionary chain. Its effect is to convert the Pokémon's sound-based attacks into Water-type maneuvers. An accompanying table details the specific moves influenced by Liquid Voice, as well as the Pokémon that inherently possess this Ability and can learn those particular moves. While Liquid Voice also modifies certain other sound-based techniques, no Pokémon inherently equipped with this Ability can learn them. However, these moves can be invoked via mechanics like Metronome, Mirror Move, Copycat, or Mimic. Furthermore, a Pokémon might employ them if it acquired Liquid Voice through another Ability, for instance Trace or Receiver, or through actions like Skill Swap or Role Play.

Title: Triage (Ability)

Known in Japanese as ヒーリングシフト (Healing Shift), Triage is an Ability introduced in Generation VII. It serves as the signature Ability for the Pokémon Comfey. This Ability significantly boosts the priority of any HP-restoring move performed by the Pokémon possessing it, increasing it by 3. This priority enhancement applies universally to both damaging attacks and status moves that replenish health. However, Triage's effect does not extend to Aqua Ring, Grassy Terrain, Ingrain, Leech Seed, Pain Split, Present, Pollen Puff, or Z-Moves that provide healing solely due to their Z-Power effect (such as Z-Conversion 2). While a supplementary table (not included here) typically details all moves influenced by Triage, as well as Pokémon capable of having Triage and learning those moves, it's worth noting that some Triage-affected moves cannot currently be learned by any Pokémon naturally endowed with this Ability. These particular moves can, however, be effectively utilized with Triage's boosted priority if the Ability is gained through external means like Trace or moves such as Skill Swap or Role Play.

Title: Galvanize (Ability)

The Ability known as Galvanize (エ レキスキン, or Electric Skin, in Japanese) first appeared in Generation VII. It is the signature Ability exclusively belonging to Alolan Geodude's evolutionary family. When a Pokémon possesses Galvanize, any Normal-type moves it employs are transformed into Electric-type attacks and gain a 20% increase in their base power. Such Normal-type attacks, having been converted to Electric-type, are then capable of triggering effects like Lightning Rod, Volt Absorb, and Motor Drive. Should an attack influenced by Galvanize be executed within Electric Terrain, it benefits from an additional 30% power surge from the terrain effect (previously a 50% boost before Generation VIII). A subsequent table details which moves are impacted by Galvanize, alongside the Pokémon capable of having Galvanize and learning those specific moves. While the following listed moves are indeed subject to this Ability's effects, no Pokémon naturally possessing Galvanize can presently learn them. Nevertheless, these moves might still be utilized through actions like Metronome, Mirror Move, Copycat, or Mimic, or by a Pokémon that acquired Galvanize from another Ability (e.g., Trace, Receiver) or a move (e.g., Skill Swap, Role Play).

Title: Schooling (Ability)

The Ability known as Schooling (Japanese: ぎょぐん Schooling) first appeared in Generation VII. This specific Ability is unique to Wishiwashi. A Wishiwashi transforms into its School Form upon entering battle or at the conclusion of a turn, provided its level is 20 or greater and its HP remains above 25%. Conversely, should its HP drop to 25% or less at the end of a turn, it reverts to its Solo Form. When Schooling is present on the target, moves such as Gastro Acid, Worry Seed, and Simple Beam are ineffective. Furthermore, Role Play, Skill Swap, Entrainment, and Doodle are unsuccessful if either participant in the battle has Schooling. Schooling is impervious to copying attempts by Trace, Power of Alchemy, or Receiver. It resists replacement by Mummy or Lingering Aroma, and similarly cannot be suppressed by Core Enforcer or Neutralizing Gas. Should Schooling be gained by any Pokémon besides Wishiwashi via Imposter or Transform, the form-changing mechanism will not occur. Uniquely among all Abilities, Schooling demands a particular level threshold for its functionality.

Title: Disguise (Ability)

This entry focuses on the Pokémon Ability known as Disguise. For information regarding Team Rocket's various disguises, please refer to the List of Team Rocket's disguises. Disguise (Japanese: ばけのかわ Disguise), an Ability introduced in Generation VII, serves as the exclusive signature trait of the Pokémon Mimikyu. When a Mimikyu, while in its Disguised Form, is struck by a damaging attack or inflicts damage upon itself due to confusion, this Ability intervenes by preventing the standard damage calculation formula from being invoked. Consequently, the incoming move deals no damage, and its type effectiveness is not computed. An exception occurs if Mimikyu is immune to the move type, in which case Disguise does not activate because the attack does not register as a hit. Upon Disguise's activation, a message stating, "Its disguise served it as a decoy!" appears, Mimikyu transitions into its Busted Form, and subsequently, the announcement, "<Name>'s disguise was busted!" is shown. Should Mimikyu's type have been altered prior to this event, it reverts to its original Ghost/Fairy typing upon assuming Busted Form. Mimikyu maintains its Busted Form even after being withdrawn and sent back into battle, but it will transform back into Disguised Form when outside of combat. If Mimikyu is knocked out and later revived, it will return in its Disguised Form, making Disguise available for use once more.

Disguise offers no protection against status-category moves, the effects of entry hazards, or environmental damage from weather conditions. For multi-strike moves, such as Water Shuriken, Disguise will only activate on the initial hit, preventing damage from that first strike but allowing subsequent strikes to inflict damage normally. It is important to note that Disguise solely blocks a move's damage; any additional effects associated with damaging moves, like the paralysis caused by Nuzzle, are not prevented. If Mimikyu is shielded by a substitute, the substitute will absorb damage before Disguise can take effect. Because an attack that busts Disguise bypasses both the type effectiveness check and the full damage formula, the held item Weakness Policy will not activate, regardless of the attacking move's type. An Air Balloon held by Mimikyu will still burst, even if Disguise negates the damage from the move that pops it. Furthermore, breaking Mimikyu's Disguise with the moves Rollout or Ice Ball is known to trigger the Rollout storage glitch.

Several Abilities and moves interact uniquely with Disguise. Gastro Acid, Worry Seed, and Simple Beam will fail when targeting a Pokémon with the Disguise Ability. Similarly, Role Play, Skill Swap, Entrainment, and Doodle cannot be successfully used if either of the involved Pokémon possesses Disguise. Disguise cannot be duplicated by Abilities such as Trace, Power of Alchemy, or Receiver. It also resists being replaced by Mummy or Lingering Aroma, traded via Wandering Spirit, or suppressed by Core Enforcer or Neutralizing Gas; should a Pokémon pass a suppression effect to a Disguise user through Baton Pass, that effect will immediately dissipate. If Mimikyu gains Disguise through Abilities like Imposter or Transform, the acquired Ability will never activate.

Certain Abilities and attacks are capable of bypassing Disguise entirely. Pokémon possessing Mold Breaker, Teravolt, or Turboblaze will disregard Disguise, striking through it without causing the form to bust. This same "ignore Disguise" property applies to the moves Moongeist Beam, Sunsteel Strike, and Photon Geyser, as well as the Z-Moves Searing Sunraze Smash, Menacing Moonraze Maelstrom, and Light That Burns the Sky. As of recent generations, when a Disguised Form Mimikyu's Disguise is busted and it transitions into its Busted Form, it now incurs damage equivalent to 1/8 of its maximum HP. This damage is rounded down and does not account for any HP boosts from Dynamax. If Mimikyu faints as a direct result of this 1/8 maximum HP damage, no additional special events occur.

Specific G-Max moves—G-Max Drum Solo, G-Max Fireball, and G-Max Hydrosnipe—are also capable of ignoring Disguise. In Tera Raid Battles, if Disguise on a Disguised Form Mimikyu absorbs a damaging move, the player's Tera Orb will not receive a charge. In Pokémon Legends: Z-A, despite the absence of Abilities, any attack hitting a Mimikyu in its Disguised Form will still only deal damage equal to 1/8 of its maximum health, causing it to change into its Busted Form. In this specific game, busting Mimikyu's disguise will also interrupt its current action. Finally, when outside of active combat and within its Poké Ball, Mimikyu will revert to its Disguised Form.

Title: Battle Bond (Ability)

Introduced in Generation VII, Battle Bond (Japanese: きずなへんげ, meaning "Bond Transformation") is an event-exclusive Ability. It functions as Greninja's signature Ability. When a Greninja possessing Battle Bond directly causes another Pokémon (including allies) to faint with a damaging move, provided this action does not end the battle, it will transform into Ash-Greninja. Following the battle, the Pokémon invariably returns to its original state. Ash-Greninja possesses superior base stats compared to a regular Greninja. Should Ash-Greninja utilize Water Shuriken, the move's power increases to 20 (from its standard 15) and it is guaranteed to hit three times. If a Pokémon uses Transform to become Ash-Greninja, Battle Bond does not influence the transformed Pokémon's execution of Water Shuriken. This Ability can be activated by multiple Greninja within the same battle. If Ash-Greninja faints during combat, it will revert to its original form, and that specific Greninja cannot change into Ash-Greninja again for the duration of that battle, even after being revived.

Gastro Acid, Worry Seed, and Simple Beam will fail if their target has Battle Bond. Role Play, Skill Swap, Entrainment, and Doodle will also fail if either participant has Battle Bond. Battle Bond cannot be copied by Trace, Power of Alchemy, or Receiver. Furthermore, it cannot be replaced by Mummy or Lingering Aroma, nor can it be suppressed by Core Enforcer or Neutralizing Gas. If a Pokémon other than Greninja acquires Battle Bond through Imposter or Transform, it cannot transform into Ash-Greninja even if it causes another Pokémon to faint.

Battle Bond cannot be legitimately observed in Generation VIII, as Greninja is unavailable. The Ability's effect has since changed: Battle Bond no longer transforms Greninja into Ash-Greninja. Instead, when a Pokémon with Battle Bond directly causes another Pokémon (including allies) to faint with a damaging move, its Attack, Special Attack, and Speed stats each increase by one stage. This stat-boosting effect can only trigger once per battle. If these aforementioned stats are already at their maximum of +6 stages, Battle Bond will not activate. Water Shuriken is no longer impacted by Battle Bond. Greninja with this Ability are unable to breed and cannot be used in Battle Spot when Special Pokémon are banned. However, they are permissible for use in battle facilities. In the Japan Mini-volume 6 of the X & Y arc, Y's Greninja, Croaky, was revealed to possess Battle Bond as his Ability.

Title: Power Construct (Ability)

The Ability known as Power Construct (スワームチェンジ, or Swarm Change, in Japanese) first appeared in Generation VII. It stands as one of Zygarde's unique signature Abilities. Should a Zygarde in its 10% or 50% Forme, possessing Power Construct, have its HP fall below half by the conclusion of a turn, it will transform into its Complete Forme. Given that Zygarde Complete Forme boasts a superior base HP stat, the Pokémon's maximum HP simultaneously rises, and its present HP value is adjusted to the new maximum HP reduced by the exact amount of HP lost prior to its transformation. Furthermore, its type specification reverts to Dragon/Ground, assuming it had been altered by an external effect.

Upon a battle's conclusion, Zygarde reverts to its initial Forme from the start of combat, carrying over its HP total from the battle's end. If this inherited HP surpasses the original Forme's maximum HP capacity, its HP is instead set to that Forme's maximum. Moves such as Gastro Acid, Worry Seed, and Simple Beam prove ineffective when targeting a Pokémon with the Power Construct Ability. Similarly, Role Play, Skill Swap, Entrainment, and Doodle cannot be successfully used if either of the involved Pokémon possesses Power Construct. Abilities like Trace, Power of Alchemy, and Receiver are unable to replicate Power Construct. Nor can Power Construct be overwritten by Mummy or Lingering Aroma, nullified by Core Enforcer or Neutralizing Gas, or exchanged via Wandering Spirit. The augmented base HP is not classified as a healing effect, meaning Heal Block does not impede it. Should a Pokémon besides Zygarde acquire Power Construct through Imposter or Transform, that Pokémon will be unable to undergo Forme changes.

In Pokémon Legends: Z-A, Abilities are not a gameplay feature. Nevertheless, in that title, Zygarde's 10% and 50% Formes still evolve into Complete Forme when their HP falls to half or less, resulting in an increased maximum HP and a concurrent gain of current HP equivalent to the maximum HP increase. If Zygarde's HP drops beneath this threshold during a move's execution, its transformation will occur upon the move's completion. During its transition into Complete Forme, Zygarde becomes invulnerable. When Zygarde is recalled outside of combat, it reverts to its prior Forme, keeping the HP it possessed at the moment of recall. Should this HP exceed the maximum for its original Forme, its HP total will be reset to that maximum.

A Zygarde equipped with Power Construct cannot be deconstructed back into individual Zygarde Cores and Cells; yet, the Zygarde Cube provides a means to alternate such a Zygarde between its 10% and 50% Formes. Exclusively within Generation VIII, the Zygarde Cube enables Zygarde to swap its Ability between Aura Break and Power Construct; across all titles, however, Zygarde is unable to modify its Ability using an Ability Capsule or an Ability Patch. Visually, the transformation depicts innumerable Zygarde Cells alongside a handful of Zygarde Cores coalescing into Zygarde.

Title: Corrosion (Ability)

This particular Ability, known as Corrosion (ふしょく in Japanese, also "Corrosion"), made its debut in Generation VII of the Pokémon series. Before Generation IX, it was exclusively associated with the Pokémon Salandit and Salazzle as their signature Ability. Its primary effect is to grant the user the capability to apply the poison status condition to any Pokémon, irrespective of their elemental type, meaning it can affect even those of the Poison- or Steel-type, which are typically immune. (It's important to note that this does not override Steel-type Pokémon's inherent immunity to damage from Poison-type attacks.)

When a Pokémon possesses Corrosion, it can successfully poison creatures of the Poison- or Steel-type through specific methods: by employing Baneful Bunker, by using Psycho Shift while already afflicted by poison, or by utilizing Fling when equipped with either a Toxic Orb or a Poison Barb. Furthermore, should a Pokémon with Corrosion execute G-Max Malodor, it gains the power to poison all opposing Pokémon on the target's side of the battlefield, even if they are of the Poison- or Steel-type (a noteworthy detail given Steel-types' resistance to Poison-type techniques).

Should a Pokémon of the Poison- or Steel-type also have Corrosion and be holding a Toxic Orb, it will nevertheless suffer the badly poisoned status itself. However, Corrosion is unable to circumvent other protective maneuvers or Abilities designed to prevent poisoning, such as Safeguard or Immunity. This Ability exhibits no influence over the entry hazard Toxic Spikes.

If a Pokémon equipped with Corrosion employs Magic Coat to bounce back a status-inflicting move that causes poison, that returned move will then possess the capability to poison Pokémon of the Poison- or Steel-type. Conversely, if a move initiated by a Pokémon possessing Corrosion is subsequently reflected by either Magic Coat or Magic Bounce, that particular reflected move will lose the special property of poisoning Poison- or Steel-type Pokémon. Finally, when a Poison- or Steel-type Pokémon with Corrosion poisons an opponent that has the Synchronize Ability, Synchronize itself does not acquire the extended capability to poison other Poison- or Steel-type Pokémon.

Title: Comatose (Ability)

This ability, known in Japanese as ぜったいねむり (Sure Sleeper), was first introduced in Generation VII. It is the signature Ability exclusively belonging to Komala. A Pokémon possessing Comatose functions as if under the sleep status, yet it does not genuinely have the status ailment itself. Such a Pokémon retains full access to its moves, even being able to execute Sleep Talk and Snore effectively. It gains immunity to non-volatile status conditions and cannot be made drowsy by Yawn. Creatures with Comatose suffer doubled damage from Hex and Wake-Up Slap. They are susceptible to Dream Eater, Nightmare, and the effects of Bad Dreams, but are unable to successfully utilize Rest.

Despite the "asleep" treatment, because the sleep status condition is not genuinely active, Pokémon with Comatose are not counted as having a status condition for various mechanics. These include effects like Purify, the consumption of Chesto Berries and Lum Berries, the move Beat Up, and the status modifier used in catch rate calculations. Comatose remains impervious to abilities or moves that typically prevent sleep, such as Uproar, Electric Terrain, and Sweet Veil. Abilities like Mold Breaker, Turboblaze, and Teravolt have no effect on Comatose. Even if a Pokémon with Poison Touch uses Sunsteel Strike, it cannot poison a Comatose-wielding target. Moves like Gastro Acid, Worry Seed, and Simple Beam will not succeed if their target possesses Comatose. Role Play, Skill Swap, Entrainment, and Doodle are unsuccessful if either the user or the target Pokémon has Comatose.

It cannot be replicated by abilities such as Trace, Power of Alchemy, or Receiver.
