Furthermore, Comatose resists being overwritten by Mummy or Lingering Aroma, suppressed by Core Enforcer or Neutralizing Gas, or exchanged via Wandering Spirit. Should a Pokémon with a suppressed ability transfer that suppression to a Comatose Pokémon using Baton Pass, the suppression effect will dissipate. Conversely, if a Pokémon whose ability is already suppressed acquires Comatose through Transform, Comatose's inherent effects will also be suppressed (meaning the Pokémon loses its status condition immunity, is not treated as asleep for moves like Sleep Talk, and so forth). Should a Pokémon already affected by a status condition acquire Comatose (for instance, via Transform or Imposter), its existing status ailment will not be removed. If the Pokémon was specifically asleep, that sleep condition will function normally, entirely independent of Comatose.

In line with the Dream Ball's revised catch rate multiplier, a 4x bonus is granted when attempting to capture a wild Pokémon possessing the Comatose ability. Nevertheless, this catch rate bonus could not be legitimately observed prior to Pokémon Scarlet and Violet, because Komala – the sole legitimate wielder of Comatose – was unavailable in games released after the Dream Ball's update until these specific titles.

Title: Queenly Majesty (Ability)

An Ability originating in Generation VII is Queenly Majesty (known as じょおうのいげん Queen's Majesty in Japanese). This unique Ability belongs to Tsareena. Should a foe employ a high-priority move – including those enhanced by Abilities like Prankster, Gale Wings, or Triage – aimed at the Pokémon possessing Queenly Majesty or its partners, Queenly Majesty will intercept and stop the execution of that move, though its PP will still be consumed. Consequently, foes are restricted to targeting the Queenly Majesty holder or its allies solely with moves that have either low priority or standard priority. However, Queenly Majesty is ineffective against moves targeting all Pokémon (with the specific exceptions of Perish Song, Flower Shield, and Rototiller) or moves affecting the opponent's side of the field, even if these moves gain increased priority. The Ability provides no interference with high-priority moves executed by allies. Z-Moves classified as status moves that possess increased priority will still successfully trigger their Z-Power bonus effects. Illustratively, when Z-Baby-Doll Eyes is directed at a target protected by Queenly Majesty, the attacking Pokémon will still receive the Defense boost, yet the target's Attack will not be reduced. Abilities such as Mold Breaker, Turboblaze, and Teravolt are capable of bypassing Queenly Majesty. When Instruct is used to call moves originally possessing increased priority, those moves maintain their initial priority and are consequently prevented by Queenly Majesty. Conversely, moves with standard or decreased priority that are invoked via an Instruct with increased priority (for example, by an attacker with Prankster) likewise preserve their initial priority and are therefore not impeded. Queenly Majesty cannot stop high-priority moves that are brought forth by other moves which inherently call additional moves. However, should a move that summons other moves be employed with increased priority itself, Queenly Majesty *will* prevent the subsequently called move, irrespective of that called move's default priority.

In the distinct context of Pokémon UNITE, Tsareena's Ability is also Queenly Majesty. Upon suffering a hindrance, the duration of that effect is reduced. Executing a boosted attack or a move awards the user a single stack of Queenly Majesty. Once three stacks accumulate, a temporary Queenly Majesty buff is bestowed upon the user, enabling the re-utilization of one of their moves (these subsequent uses operate on separate cooldowns from the base moves), resulting in heightened damage and a supplementary effect determined by the specific move employed.

Title: Innards Out (Ability)

The Ability known as Innards Out (Japanese: とびだすなかみ, translated as Flying Innards) made its debut in Generation VII. It serves as the exclusive signature Ability of Pyukumuku. Should a Pokémon possessing this Ability be incapacitated by an opposing Pokémon's offensive maneuver, it retaliates by inflicting damage upon that assailant. This damage precisely matches the HP value the user had just prior to sustaining the final blow.

In instances where a Pokémon equipped with Innards Out succumbs to the delayed effects of Future Sight or Doom Desire, the Ability's activation is contingent upon the original user of that move still being present on the battlefield. Furthermore, if a Pokémon with this Ability moves first and is subsequently knocked out by Core Enforcer, Innards Out will fail to trigger. In a scenario where Innards Out causes two opposing Pokémon to faint simultaneously, and neither Trainer possesses further Pokémon, the Trainer whose Pokémon triggered Innards Out is declared the loser. When a Pokémon with this Ability is rendered unconscious by a multi-strike move (including those made multi-hit by Parental Bond), the full combined HP from every strike is totaled and then dealt back as a single burst of damage to the attacker.

Title: Dancer (Ability)

The Ability known as Dancer (Japanese: おどりこ Dancer) debuted in Generation VII. Oricorio uniquely possesses this specific capability. Any time another Pokémon executes a dance category move, a Pokémon possessing the Dancer Ability will promptly replicate that same move. A move performed through Dancer constitutes an action distinct from the one initially chosen. Dancer's effect does not trigger if a move is mimicked by another Pokémon also equipped with Dancer; however, it *will* activate when responding to an instructed dance move. Even if a status dance move is amplified into its Z-Move equivalent (such as Z-Feather Dance), Dancer can still replicate it; nonetheless, the Pokémon with Dancer will perform the standard variant of the move, foregoing the enhanced Z-Power bonus.

The Dancer Ability will not initiate if every one of the move's intended targets is shielded from it, if the move is unsuccessful in affecting any Pokémon whatsoever (for instance, Teeter Dance where all targets are already confused or possess Own Tempo), or if all targets inherently resist it (like an Electric-type Revelation Dance against a Ground-type foe). Furthermore, Dancer remains dormant should the move be intercepted by Snatch, or if the Dancer-wielding Pokémon is within the semi-invulnerable phase of an action such as Fly.

Should several Pokémon possess Dancer simultaneously when a dance move is performed, the Pokémon with the lowest Speed stat will act first (ignoring the effects of Lagging Tail and Full Incense), a rule that holds true even under the influence of Trick Room. A Pokémon afflicted by confusion, when attempting to copy a move via Dancer, might inflict self-damage instead, even if safeguarded by defensive moves like Protect or Mat Block. Similarly, a Pokémon that has flinched will experience this same limitation when later attempting to replicate moves using Dancer.

A Dancer-enabled Pokémon, if constrained by a consecutively repeating move (such as Petal Dance), or by Encore, or a held Choice item, will still attempt to copy an incoming dance move. This attempt will only succeed if the Pokémon is already locked into that *exact* same dance move; for instance, if Petal Dance is used through Dancer while the Pokémon is locked into Petal Dance, this specific instance does not contribute to the 2-3 turn lock duration. Despite holding an Assault Vest, a Pokémon with Dancer remains capable of successfully mimicking status dance moves. The move Lunar Dance is replicated only *after* its initial performer has fainted. Should a Pokémon mirror Petal Dance through Dancer, it will not become confined to using that move consecutively. When Feather Dance is sent back by Magic Bounce or Magic Coat, Dancer will not activate, neither for the original execution of the move nor for its bounced-back application. Even if subjected to Taunt, a Dancer-equipped Pokémon will still try to replicate a status dance move, yet it will be unsuccessful.

Conversely, moves executed through Dancer are susceptible to being pilfered by Snatch and bounced back by Magic Bounce and Magic Coat. Actions performed via Dancer are not counted as the most recent move employed (for mechanics like Instruct, Mimic, or Mirror Move), but any damage they inflict *is* factored in for moves such as Counter, Mirror Coat, Metal Burst, and Comeuppance. In the context of a Double Battle, if a teammate employs a single-target dance move against an adversary, the replicated move by Dancer will similarly target that identical foe. Otherwise, a single-target dance move that is copied will direct itself toward the original user of the dance move. Notably, during a Tera Raid Battle, Dancer's activation is suppressed if an allied Pokémon performs a dance move.

Title: Battery (Ability)
This entry describes the Ability; for details concerning the held item, refer to Cell Battery. Debuting in Generation VII, Battery (Japanese: バッテリー Battery) is an Ability exclusively held by Charjabug. When allied Pokémon use special moves, this Ability significantly enhances their Special Attack stat, providing a precise multiplier of 5325/4096, which approximates a 30% increase. Professor Kukui discussed Battery's function with his students in class, as documented in the episode So Long, Sophocles!. Furthermore, Battery holds the distinction of being one of just four signature Abilities, along with Honey Gather, Wimp Out, and Ball Fetch, to have been introduced solely for a pre-evolved Pokémon.

Title: Fluffy (Ability)

Fluffy (Japanese: もふもふ Fluffy) is an Ability that first appeared in Generation VII. Prior to Generation VIII, it was the signature Ability of Stufful and Bewear. In Generation IX, by contrast, it became the exclusive trait of Greavard and Houndstone. A Pokémon endowed with Fluffy will sustain half the damage from moves that involve physical contact. Conversely, it incurs twice the standard damage from Fire-type attacks. If a Fire-type move also makes physical contact, it will inflict regular damage. Moreover, attacks influenced by Long Reach that nevertheless make contact will deal normal damage.

Title: Dazzling (Ability)

The Ability Dazzling (Japanese: ビビッドボディ Vivid Body) was introduced in Generation VII. It is the signature Ability of Bruxish. When an opposing Pokémon attempts to use a high-priority move (including those boosted by Prankster, Gale Wings, or Triage) targeting the Dazzling Pokémon or its allies, the Ability intervenes, causing the move to fail after its PP has been deducted. As a result, the adversary can only successfully target the Dazzling Pokémon or its companions with moves of decreased or standard priority.

Dazzling does not block moves that affect all Pokémon (with the exceptions of Perish Song, Flower Shield, and Rototiller) or moves that target the opponent's side of the field, even if such moves gain increased priority. Allies' moves with elevated priority are unaffected by Dazzling. Status Z-Moves that possess increased priority will still have their Z-Power effect activate. For example, if Z-Baby-Doll Eyes is used on a Pokémon protected by Dazzling, the user will still gain Defense, though the target's Attack will not be lowered.

Mold Breaker, Turboblaze, and Teravolt ignore this Ability. Moves with increased priority that are called by Instruct retain their original priority and are consequently blocked by Dazzling. Conversely, moves with decreased or no priority, even when called by an Instruct that possesses increased priority (e.g., from a Prankster user), similarly preserve their original priority status and are not blocked. High-priority moves that are called using any other "calling" moves cannot be obstructed by Dazzling. However, if a move that calls other moves is executed with increased priority, Dazzling will prevent the subsequently called move, regardless of that move's inherent priority.

Title: Receiver (Ability)

Originating in Generation VII, Receiver (レシーバー in Japanese) functions as the unique signature Ability of the Pokémon Passimian. Should an allied Pokémon be knocked out during combat, regardless of the reason for its defeat, the Pokémon possessing Receiver will have this Ability swapped out for the fallen ally's Ability. However, this transfer mechanism will not engage if the ally that fainted possessed any of the following Abilities: Receiver, Power of Alchemy, Trace, Forecast, Flower Gift, Multitype, Illusion, Wonder Guard, Zen Mode, Imposter, Stance Change, Power Construct, Schooling, Comatose, Shields Down, Disguise, RKS System, Battle Bond, Wandering Spirit, Gulp Missile, Ice Face, Hunger Switch, As One, Zero to Hero, Commander, Protosynthesis, or Quark Drive. Furthermore, Receiver resists being replicated by Abilities such as Role Play or Trace. A Pokémon with Receiver attempting to use Role Play or Entrainment will find these moves unsuccessful. An update introduced with Version 3.0.0 of Pokémon Scarlet and Violet established that Gulp Missile can now successfully replace Receiver.

Title: Beast Boost (Ability)

Known in Japanese as ビーストブースト (Beast Boost), this Ability debuted in Generation VII. It serves as the exclusive signature power of the Ultra Beasts. Should a Pokémon possessing Beast Boost directly incapacitate another combatant (even an ally) through the application of a damaging technique, its most elevated stat (excluding HP) receives a single-stage boost for every Pokémon that faints from that specific move's use. However, if the chosen stat has already reached its maximum of +6 stages, Beast Boost fails to trigger, irrespective of whether multiple stats are tied for the highest. When identifying the highest stat, Beast Boost disregards existing stat modifiers, equipped items, or any stat decreases stemming from status ailments. Nevertheless, it does factor in the repercussions of moves like Power Split, Guard Split, Power Trick, Wonder Room, and Speed Swap. Should multiple stats share the distinction of being the highest, the Ability will enhance one of them according to a strict priority sequence: Attack, then Defense, followed by Special Attack, Special Defense, and finally Speed. Furthermore, if the defeated Pokémon's collapse concludes the ongoing battle, Beast Boost will not come into effect. Its activation sequence places it subsequent to any Attack gains conferred by the move Fell Stinger. In a scenario where a Beast Boost user vanquishes a foe possessing Mummy via a contact move, the user's Ability will transform into Mummy prior to Beast Boost having a chance to manifest. Notably, Sun's Stakataka, named Drachma, was publicly confirmed to possess Beast Boost as its characteristic power.

Title: Misty Surge (Ability)

First appearing in Generation VII, Misty Surge (known in Japanese as ミストメイカー or Mist Maker) is an Ability. Prior to Generation VIII, it functioned as the exclusive signature Ability of Tapu Fini. However, by Generation IX, this distinction transferred to Galarian Weezing, for whom it now serves as a signature capability. Upon a Pokémon possessing Misty Surge entering combat, the battlefield immediately becomes imbued with the effects of the move Misty Terrain. Any accompanying statistical figures denote precise, pre-set values, rather than conventional base stats. These figures are custom-assigned and not derived through calculations based on base stats, level, Nature, Individual Values (IVs), and Effort Values (EVs).

Title: Grassy Surge (Ability)
An Ability introduced in Generation VII, Grassy Surge is known in Japanese as グラスメイカー (Grass Maker). Before Generation VIII, it served as the signature Ability for Tapu Bulu. As of Generation IX, it has become the distinctive Ability of Grookey's evolutionary line. The moment a Pokémon with Grassy Surge enters combat, the battlefield is instantly affected by the move Grassy Terrain. This particular Ability is exceptional, being the sole terrain-creating one accessible to more than two Pokémon species. Moreover, it was notably the only such Ability that could not be acquired upon the initial release of Pokémon Sword and Shield.

Title: Full Metal Body (Ability)

Known as メタルプロテクト (Metal Protect) in Japanese, Full Metal Body was first introduced as an Ability in Generation VII. It serves as the signature capability of Solgaleo. This Ability provides immunity to stat reduction caused by other Pokémon's moves and Abilities, encompassing examples such as Scary Face, Intimidate, and even the entry hazard Sticky Web. Crucially, Full Metal Body does not prevent stat reductions that are self-inflicted, such as those from using moves like Superpower or Shell Smash. The protection offered by Full Metal Body is specific to effects that lower *stat stages*. As such, it offers no defense against stat decreases resulting from held items (e.g., the Iron Ball), status conditions (like paralysis or burn), or the direct effects of moves such as Guard Split or Power Split. Similarly, Full Metal Body does not impede stat stages from being directly modified by moves including Haze, Clear Smog, Heart Swap, Guard Swap, Power Swap, Baton Pass, or Topsy-Turvy. Furthermore, it offers no safeguard against Spectral Thief stealing (i.e., resetting) positive stat changes. Unlike White Smoke and Clear Body, Full Metal Body cannot be ignored by other moves or Abilities, though it can still be changed or suppressed.

Title: Shadow Shield (Ability)
This Ability, known as ファントムガード (Phantom Guard) in Japanese, debuted in Generation VII. It is the distinctive Ability of Lunala, making it unique to that Pokémon. While a Pokémon bearing Shadow Shield maintains its maximum HP, incoming damage from offensive moves is reduced by fifty percent. Nevertheless, its effect does not extend to attacks that cause direct, fixed damage. Should the Pokémon be struck by a multi-hit technique while at its highest HP, only the very first impact will see its damage lessened. Every following hit in the sequence will then deliver its complete, unaltered damage. Distinct from Multiscale, this Ability cannot be circumvented by any moves or other Abilities. Despite this, it remains susceptible to alteration or temporary suppression.

Title: Prism Armor (Ability)

This Ability, known in Japanese as プリズムアーマー Prism Armor, made its debut in Generation VII. It stands among Necrozma's unique signature Abilities. Prism Armor causes damage from supereffective attacks to be reduced by 25%, regardless of the specific effectiveness multiplier. For instance, a move that would typically inflict 2× damage will instead inflict 1.5× damage. Unlike Solid Rock and Filter, this Ability is impervious to being ignored by other moves or Abilities. Nevertheless, much like Solid Rock and Filter, its effects can still be altered or suppressed.

Title: Libero (Ability)

The Ability known as Libero (Japanese: リベロ リベロ) was introduced in Generation VIII. It is exclusively the signature Ability of the Scorbunny evolutionary line. Immediately preceding the execution of any move (excluding Struggle), a Pokémon with Libero will transform its own type to match the type of the move it is about to perform. Libero invariably results in the user becoming a single-type Pokémon.

Because Libero's activation occurs prior to a move's execution, the Pokémon gains the same-type attack bonus on every move it utilizes (except Struggle), irrespective of that move's original type, and ensures that the move Toxic will always connect. When employing a move that calls another move (such as Nature Power), the type of the called move will be taken into consideration. If a move itself can alter its type or has been affected by Electrify, the type it changes to is the one Libero considers. For moves that modify the user's type, like Reflect Type, Libero first changes the user's type to the move's type, after which the move will either fail or subsequently re-alter the user's type.

Regarding Curse, unless its type has been changed by Electrify, if the user is not already a Ghost-type before Libero activates, Libero will transform the user into a Ghost-type. The user will then execute the Ghost-type effect of Curse on itself, regardless of Follow Me, Rage Powder, or Crafty Shield.

Libero will not activate if the move's execution is entirely interrupted and its name isn't announced (for instance, due to infatuation or confusion), if the move is prevented by effects such as Powder, heavy rain, extremely harsh sunlight, Dazzling, or Queenly Majesty, or if the user is already the identical single type as the move being used. Conversely, Libero will trigger even if the move misses, has no effect due to the target's type, or is blocked by a protection move. Libero generally activates even if the move fails.

However, a specific set of moves conducts a success check before Libero activates; if these moves fail, they prevent Libero from taking effect. These include:
- Counter, Mirror Coat, and Metal Burst (when the user hasn't been hit by an attack)
- Explosion, Self-Destruct, Mind Blown, and Misty Explosion (if Damp is active on a Pokémon)
- Rest (if the user has maximum HP, is sleeping, or holds Insomnia, Vital Spirit, or Comatose)
- Teleport (if no allies are present, or all allies have fainted)
- Protection moves (if the user acted last or executed a protection move successfully in the previous turn)
- Destiny Bond (if the user successfully executed Destiny Bond in the previous turn)
- Future Sight and Doom Desire (if the target is already marked by Future Sight or Doom Desire)
- Fake Out, Mat Block, and First Impression (if it's not the user's initial turn)
- Follow Me and Rage Powder (in a single battle)
- Spit Up and Swallow (if the user possesses no stockpiles)
- Last Resort (if the user hasn't used all other moves, knows only Last Resort, or doesn't know Last Resort but used it by calling)
- Sucker Punch (if the target has already moved or did not choose an attacking move)
- Clangorous Soul (if the user lacks the necessary HP)
- No Retreat (if the user has already successfully performed No Retreat)

The user's newly acquired type endures until it is altered again or until the Pokémon is withdrawn from battle; neither negating nor replacing the Ability will restore the user to their original type. Libero functions a maximum of once per Pokémon entry into battle. If the user Terastallizes, Libero's effects are nullified, rendering the Ability ineffective on a Terastallized Pokémon. The Ability's nomenclature potentially alludes to the libero position in association football, which is also commonly known as the sweeper or center-back.

Title: Ball Fetch (Ability)

Ball Fetch, known in Japanese as たまひろい (Ball Fetch), is an Ability that made its introduction in Generation VIII. It functions as the exclusive signature Ability of Yamper. In any battle, following the moment the first Poké Ball is deployed and fails to secure a Pokémon, a specific event can transpire. At the conclusion of that turn, if a Pokémon possessing Ball Fetch is currently active on the field and not already equipped with an item, it will retrieve the identical variety of ball that was originally thrown. This retrieval mechanism is restricted to a single activation per battle. Ball Fetch shares a unique distinction with Honey Gather, Battery, and Wimp Out, as it is one of just four signature Abilities to have been assigned exclusively to a pre-evolved Pokémon upon its initial appearance.

Title: Cotton Down (Ability)

Cotton Down (Japanese: わたげ Cotton Down) is an Ability that made its debut in Generation VIII. It serves as the exclusive Ability for Gossifleur and Eldegoss. When a Pokémon endowed with this Ability is struck by an offensive move, the Speed stat of all other Pokémon on the field is reduced by one stage. Should a Pokémon possessing Cotton Down be hit by a move that strikes multiple times (such as Fury Swipes), each individual strike will trigger the Ability's effect.

In the separate game of Pokémon UNITE, Cotton Down is also Eldegoss's unique Ability. When Eldegoss accrues a particular amount of damage, the Ability causes it to restore its own HP, retaliate with damage, and momentarily lower the movement speed of opposing Pokémon. This iteration of the Ability is subject to a 10-second cooldown period.

Title: Mirror Armor (Ability)

The Ability known as Mirror Armor (Japanese: ミラーアーマー Mirror Armor) was first introduced in Generation VIII. It serves as Corviknight's signature Ability. Mirror Armor's primary function is to return any stat-lowering effects from both moves and Abilities directly to their original user. However, it does not reflect the stat-lowering effect of Octolock, nor can it reflect an effect that was previously bounced back by an opponent's Mirror Armor. Nevertheless, stat-lowering effects of moves that have been reflected by Magic Bounce remain eligible for reflection by Mirror Armor. Should a singular effect attempt to lower the stats of multiple Pokémon, including the Pokémon holding this Ability, only the stat reduction designated for the Pokémon with Mirror Armor is reflected. When a Pokémon with this Ability is influenced by Sticky Web, the effect is returned to the Pokémon that established the entry hazard. If the Pokémon that deployed Sticky Web is no longer active in the battle, then no Pokémon will experience a Speed reduction.

Title: Gulp Missile (Ability)

Known in Japanese as うのミサイル, Gulp Missile is a unique Ability, exclusive to Cramorant, first seen in Generation VIII. When a Cramorant possessing the Gulp Missile Ability executes either Surf or Dive, it snatches a Pokémon as prey, altering its physical state based on its current health. Should Cramorant's HP exceed half its maximum, it captures an Arrokuda and adopts its Gulping Form. Conversely, if its HP falls below half, it seizes a Pikachu, shifting into its Gorging Form.

Upon sustaining damage from an incoming attack while in either of these forms, Cramorant retaliates by launching its captured prey at the aggressor. This projectile inflicts damage equivalent to one-fourth (¼) of the assailant's total HP and applies a distinct secondary status ailment or stat alteration based on the specific prey: an Arrokuda strike reduces the attacker's Defense stat by a single stage, whereas a Pikachu hit causes paralysis. Following this counterattack, Cramorant reverts to its standard base form. Even if the attacking Pokémon possesses the Magic Guard Ability, it will not suffer any damage from the retaliatory projectile; however, the visual animation (cutscene) will still play, and the Defense reduction or paralysis effect will still be applied.

Should Cramorant undergo Dynamaxing while holding prey, it reverts to its original form, refraining from spitting out its catch. Furthermore, a Cramorant that is already Dynamaxed will not adopt its Gulping or Gorging Form even if it employs Surf or Dive (a scenario exclusively observed with wild Pokémon during a Max Raid Battle).

Certain Abilities and moves encounter unique restrictions when interacting with Gulp Missile: Gastro Acid, Worry Seed, and Simple Beam are ineffective if Cramorant is the target. Role Play, Skill Swap, Entrainment, and Doodle are unsuccessful if Gulp Missile is active on either Pokémon. Moreover, Gulp Missile cannot be replicated by Trace nor can it take the place of Receiver's effect. Its functionality is unaffected by Neutralizing Gas, which cannot suppress it. Similarly, Abilities like Mummy or Lingering Aroma are incapable of replacing Gulp Missile. When a Pokémon employing Imposter mimics a Cramorant, or one utilizing Transform morphs into a Cramorant, the Gulp Missile's activation during the use of Surf or Dive will not occur.

However, with the release of Pokémon Scarlet and Violet, Version 3.0.0, the mechanics surrounding Gulp Missile were updated: it can now be copied via Trace, exchanged through Skill Swap or Wandering Spirit, and substitute Receiver.

Within the realm of Pokémon UNITE, Gulp Missile functions as Cramorant's distinct Ability. While holding prey, Cramorant automatically retaliates against enemies upon receiving damage. Alternatively, Cramorant can expend its prey as an enhanced basic attack, launching it towards an opponent; this projectile then rebounds to strike a single additional nearby foe.

Title: Steam Engine (Ability)

First appearing in Generation VIII, Steam Engine (Japanese: じょうききかん Steam Engine) is an Ability. This distinctive Ability is exclusive to Rolycoly and its evolved forms. Upon taking damage from a Fire-type or Water-type attack, a Pokémon with Steam Engine will have its Speed stat boosted by six stages. Its activation sequence places it *after* any potential stat reductions from the impacting move have taken effect. Moreover, if a Pokémon with Steam Engine is present in the party — regardless of whether it has fainted — the hatching time for all Pokémon Eggs within that party is cut in half. This specific hatching benefit does not combine with additional Steam Engine Abilities, or with Flame Body or Magma Armor.

Title: Punk Rock (Ability)

Punk Rock (Japanese: パンクロック Punk Rock) is an Ability that made its initial appearance in Generation VIII. It serves as Toxtricity's unique signature Ability. When a Pokémon possesses Punk Rock, the potency of its sound-based techniques is enhanced by 30% (specifically, 5325/4096). Moreover, a Pokémon with Punk Rock takes merely half the damage from damaging sound-based attacks. The subsequent table illustrates the moves that are influenced by Punk Rock, as well as the Pokémon capable of having Punk Rock and mastering those moves. Although some moves are affected by this Ability, they are presently not learnable by any Pokémon naturally possessing Punk Rock. Nevertheless, they can be invoked via Metronome, Copycat, or Mimic, or employed by a Pokémon that acquired Punk Rock through an Ability such as Trace or Receiver, or a move like Skill Swap or Role Play. Casey's Low Key Form Toxtricity, Tera, has been disclosed as having Punk Rock as his particular Ability.

Title: Ripen (Ability)

Ripen (Japanese: じゅくせい Ripen) is an Ability first introduced in Generation VIII. It is the exclusive Ability of Applin, Flapple, and Appletun. Ripen causes held Berries consumed during battle to yield twice their usual effect. This includes instances where a Pokémon possessing Ripen is struck by a flung Berry. The Ability enhances Berries that replenish HP or PP (e.g., Figy Berry, Leppa Berry), those mitigating damage (like an Occa Berry), stat-boosting Berries (with the exception of Lansat Berry), and Berries that inflict recoil damage upon foes striking the holder (such as a Rowap Berry). Conversely, Ripen has no impact on Berries designed to heal status conditions (such as the Persim or Lum Berry), nor does it modify the Lansat Berry (meaning it will not quadruple the critical hit stage increase), the Micle Berry, or the Custap Berry, even though a message indicating its activation may still display. Furthermore, a known glitch causes Ripen to activate visually (displaying a message and animation) without any actual effect when a Pokémon with it consumes specific non-Berry items or is targeted by a flung item possessing a secondary effect. The items impacted are listed below:

Title: Ice Face (Ability)

An Ability known as Ice Face (Japanese: アイスフェイス) made its debut in Generation VIII. This unique capability is exclusive to Eiscue. When an Eiscue in its Ice Face form takes a hit from a physical move, it sustains no damage and immediately transforms into its Noice Face form. Eiscue will restore its Ice Face form if a hailstorm or snowstorm begins while it is in its Noice Face form, or if it is sent into battle in its Noice Face form during existing hail or snow. Conversely, Eiscue will not revert to its Ice Face form if hail or snow is already active at the moment it transitions into its Noice Face form. This form alteration endures even when Eiscue is withdrawn from battle, though it resets once the battle concludes. Ice Face offers no protection against special moves, such as Psyshock, Psystrike, or Secret Sword. Gastro Acid, Worry Seed, and Simple Beam will fail if the target possesses Ice Face. Role Play, Skill Swap, Entrainment, and Doodle are unsuccessful if either Pokémon has Ice Face. Ice Face cannot be copied by Trace, nor can it supersede Power of Alchemy or Receiver. It is immune to suppression by Neutralizing Gas, cannot be traded via Wandering Spirit, and resists replacement by Lingering Aroma or Mummy. Ice Face first appeared as an Ability in the Pokémon Trading Card Game, featured on Eiscue from the Rebel Clash expansion. In the TCG, if a Pokémon with this Ability has full HP, the damage it receives from attacks by an opponent's Pokémon is lessened by a predetermined quantity (this reduction is applied after considering Weakness and Resistance). Below is a list of Pokémon cards that feature the Ice Face Ability.

Title: Power Spot (Ability)

Should you be seeking locations where Dynamaxing is achievable, consult the Dynamax entry. Introduced in Generation VIII, Power Spot (Japanese: パワースポット) is an Ability exclusive to Stonjourner. Its effect causes the power of moves unleashed by allied Pokémon to be increased by 30%. The phrase "power spot" itself denotes a location believed to possess sacred energy, often accompanied by special healing properties. This Ability aptly reflects Stonjourner, a Pokémon conceptualized from Stonehenge, a renowned historical site recognized as a power spot.

Title: Mimicry (Ability)

Known in Japanese as ぎたい (Mimicry), this Ability made its debut in Generation VIII. It is the signature characteristic exclusive to Galarian Stunfisk. Mimicry causes a Pokémon's typing to dynamically shift based on the prevailing battlefield terrain. The type transformation is as follows: while Electric Terrain is active, the Pokémon assumes a pure Electric classification. Under Grassy Terrain, its typing becomes exclusively Grass. Misty Terrain prompts a change to a pure Fairy type. Should Psychic Terrain be present, the Pokémon transitions to a pure Psychic type. Upon the cessation of the terrain, the Pokémon's inherent typing is automatically restored. (Importantly, transformed Pokémon with Mimicry revert to their *own* original typing from before transformation, not the type of the Pokémon they mimicked.) This Ability engages either when the Pokémon holding Mimicry enters the field while terrain is already present, or whenever the terrain itself changes. Any subsequent type alteration by other methods (such as the move Soak) will supersede the type imposed by Mimicry. The activation of Mimicry occurs regardless of whether the Pokémon is grounded. If the Pokémon possessing Mimicry has an additional type due to moves like Forest's Curse or Trick-or-Treat, the terrain-triggered Mimicry will generally only modify its primary types, leaving the added types unaffected. However, a specific interaction occurs if the Pokémon is already a Grass-type from Forest's Curse when Grassy Terrain causes it to become Grass-type through Mimicry; in this scenario, the effect of Forest's Curse disappears. It has been disclosed that Mega, Casey's Galarian Stunfisk, possesses Mimicry as its Ability.

Title: Wandering Spirit (Ability)

Appearing first in Generation VIII, the Ability Wandering Spirit (Japanese: さまようたましい Wandering Spirit) was introduced. This particular Ability is exclusive to Galarian Yamask and Runerigus. Upon being struck by a contact move, a Pokémon possessing Wandering Spirit will swap Abilities with the Pokémon that initiated the attack. Should a Pokémon that had its Ability changed by Wandering Spirit be withdrawn from battle, its original Ability will be restored. This Ability's effect takes place even if the Pokémon holding Wandering Spirit is knocked out by the contact move it was hit by. However, Wandering Spirit will not activate if the attacking Pokémon is in its Dynamax form. Furthermore, Wandering Spirit cannot affect or interact with the subsequent Abilities: As One, Battle Bond, Comatose, Commander, Disguise, Flower Gift, Forecast, Gulp Missile, Hunger Switch, Ice Face, Illusion, Imposter, Multitype, Neutralizing Gas, Power of Alchemy, Receiver, RKS System, Schooling, Shields Down, Stance Change, Wonder Guard, Zen Mode, and Zero to Hero.

Title: Gorilla Tactics (Ability)

Introduced in Generation VIII, the Ability known as Gorilla Tactics (Japanese: ごりむちゅう, meaning "Obsessed Gorilla") debuted. This particular Ability is a signature trait associated with Galarian Darmanitan. Gorilla Tactics provides a substantial 50% increase to a Pokémon's Attack stat. However, it concurrently imposes a restriction, compelling the Pokémon to exclusively use a single move, much like the effect of a Choice Band. This potent effect synergizes with other Choice items; for instance, combining Gorilla Tactics with a Choice Band amplifies the Pokémon's Attack stat to a total of 225%. When the user undergoes Dynamaxing, Gorilla Tactics is temporarily suppressed. The Zen Mode form of Galarian Darmanitan, upon its transformation, acquires all the Abilities of its Standard Mode counterpart. Nonetheless, this transformation itself is contingent on the Pokémon originally possessing the Zen Mode Ability. Thus, Gorilla Tactics is rendered unobtainable for this specific form. The naming of Gorilla Tactics often incorporates linguistic cleverness across various languages: The English rendition, for instance, blends "gorilla" with "guerrilla tactics." In Japanese, its designation intricately merges 五里霧中 (gorimuchū), a phrase denoting "lost in a fog," with ゴリラ (gorira), meaning "gorilla," and 夢中 (muchū), signifying "obsessed." Chinese localization substitutes the character 心 (xīn), which means "heart," within the idiom 一心一意 ("wholeheartedly") with 猩 (xīng), representing "gorilla." The Spanish title, translating literally as "monotheme," effectively conveys the Ability's single-move constraint, while also subtly integrating "mono," the Spanish term for monkey.

Title: Neutralizing Gas (Ability)

The Ability known as Neutralizing Gas (Japanese: かがくへんかガス Chemical Change Gas) first appeared in Generation VIII. It serves as the unique signature Ability for the Koffing family of Pokémon. This Ability nullifies the active effects of other Pokémon's Abilities on the battlefield, provided those Pokémon are not equipped with an Ability Shield. Upon a Pokémon with Neutralizing Gas entering combat, a notification message for the Ability is shown, occurring even prior to the activation of entry hazards.

Should Neutralizing Gas cease to be active, Abilities that trigger upon being gained (meaning Abilities that activate upon a Pokémon's entry into battle, as exemplified by Intimidate) will instantly display their activation message, irrespective of whether they had previously done so. The sole exceptions are Unnerve, which still takes effect without a message, and Imposter, which only activates when initially switched into battle, rather than when simply gained. In scenarios where Neutralizing Gas ceases to apply because its user is preparing to exit the battle, those aforementioned Abilities activate before the switch-out takes place. For instance, if Intimidate is triggered under these conditions, it will reduce the Attack stat of the Pokémon currently bearing Neutralizing Gas before its departure, instead of affecting the Attack of the Pokémon that subsequently enters the fray.

Neutralizing Gas is incapable of suppressing another instance of Neutralizing Gas itself, nor can it affect Multitype, Zen Mode, Stance Change, Power Construct, Schooling, RKS System, Shields Down, Battle Bond, Comatose, Disguise, Gulp Missile, Ice Face, As One, or Tera Shift. It resists being copied by moves such as Trace, Role Play, or Doodle. Furthermore, abilities like Skill Swap or Wandering Spirit are ineffective at exchanging Neutralizing Gas. While Entrainment will fail if the Pokémon using it possesses Neutralizing Gas, it can still succeed if the target Pokémon has Neutralizing Gas. Nonetheless, Neutralizing Gas is susceptible to being replaced (for example, by Worry Seed) or suppressed (such as through Gastro Acid), mirroring the behavior of most other Abilities, with the key distinction that it cannot be suppressed by itself or by another user of Neutralizing Gas. Curiously, its Japanese designation is identical to a Pokémon Power with a comparable operational effect.

Title: Hunger Switch (Ability)

This ability, known in Japanese as はらぺこスイッチ (Hunger Switch), made its debut in Generation VIII. It serves as Morpeko's exclusive signature ability. At the close of each turn, a Morpeko possessing Hunger Switch will alternate between its Full Belly Mode and Hangry Mode. In Full Belly Mode, Aura Wheel becomes an Electric-type move; conversely, when in Hangry Mode, it functions as a Dark-type move. Both Entrainment and Role Play will fail if used against a Pokémon with Hunger Switch. This particular ability cannot be copied by Trace, nor can it be swapped by Wandering Spirit. Furthermore, Power of Alchemy and Receiver are unable to copy Hunger Switch. Should Morpeko's Hunger Switch be nullified or replaced, the Pokémon will maintain its current form. If any Pokémon besides Morpeko obtains Hunger Switch through Transform or Imposter, it will not experience form changes. Terastallization prevents Hunger Switch from activating on Morpeko. A Terastallized Morpeko will also retain its form, even if it is withdrawn from battle. In Pokémon Legends: Z-A, abilities are not part of standard gameplay. However, Morpeko will still shift between Full Belly Mode and Hangry Mode upon using Aura Wheel in that game. Lastly, the Official Anime Pokémon Twitter officially confirmed Marnie's Morpeko to possess Hunger Switch.

Title: Quick Draw (Ability)

Known in Japanese as クイックドロウ (Quick Draw), this Ability made its debut in Generation VIII, specifically within The Isle of Armor expansion. It serves as the unique signature Ability for Galarian Slowbro. Should a Pokémon possessing Quick Draw choose a damaging attack, there is a 30% likelihood that it will execute its action ahead of others within its designated priority bracket. An on-screen notification confirms its activation at the commencement of the turn, immediately following move selection. Its activation chance operates independently from that of a held Quick Claw; however, if Quick Draw successfully triggers, the Quick Claw will not activate on that same turn. When a Pokémon holds a Quick Claw in addition to having the Quick Draw Ability and uses a damaging move, the combined chance for either effect to trigger becomes 44%. Furthermore, a held Custap Berry belonging to the Pokémon will be prevented from activating on any turn Quick Draw is successful, though it remains capable of activating on subsequent turns where Quick Draw does not trigger. In scenarios where Quick Draw or Quick Claw simultaneously activate for multiple distinct Pokémon during the same turn, the execution order of their moves is determined by their standard Speed stat within their shared priority bracket.

Title: Unseen Fist (Ability)

Known in Japanese as ふかしのこぶし (Invisible Fist), Unseen Fist is an Ability that made its debut in Generation VIII, specifically within The Isle of Armor. This particular Ability is unique to Urshifu. Unseen Fist causes the Pokémon's contact moves to penetrate target protection moves, with Max Guard being the sole exception. This piercing effect holds true even when the user is equipped with Protective Pads. However, the effect is nullified if the Pokémon wears a Punching Glove, as that item reclassifies punching moves as non-contact. Information regarding the specific moves impacted by Unseen Fist and the respective Urshifu forms that learn them is also documented. From June 11 to December 14, 2022, a programming error inadvertently allowed Galarian Slowking transferred from Pokémon GO to Pokémon HOME via the GO Transporter to obtain Unseen Fist. This fault has since been rectified, and any Slowking currently in or subsequently deposited into HOME that possesses Unseen Fist will have its Ability automatically corrected to Curious Medicine.

Title: Curious Medicine (Ability)

Known in Japan as きみょうなくすり, the Ability called Curious Medicine made its debut in Generation VIII's The Crown Tundra expansion. This distinctive power belongs exclusively to Galarian Slowking. The moment a Pokémon carrying this Ability enters a fight, it instantly resets the stat stages of its allies back to 0. From June 11 through December 14 of 2022, a software anomaly permitted Galarian Slowking, when moved from Pokémon GO to Pokémon HOME via the GO Transporter, to incorrectly manifest with the Unseen Fist Ability. The aforementioned error has since been rectified; any Slowking already present in or subsequently transferred to HOME exhibiting Unseen Fist will have its designated Ability retroactively changed to Curious Medicine.

Title: Transistor (Ability)

Transistor, also known by its Japanese name トランジスタ, is an Ability first introduced in Generation VIII's The Crown Tundra. It serves as Regieleki's signature Ability. When a Pokémon with this Ability launches an Electric-type move, its Attack or Special Attack stat receives a 1.5 multiplier during damage calculation, effectively increasing the damage dealt by 50%. However, the attacking stat multiplier has since been adjusted, now sitting at approximately 1.3 (5325/4096). Transistor is unique among Steelworker variants for not currently providing a 1.5 multiplier to attacking stats, a boost it did offer in Generation VIII.

Title: Lingering Aroma (Ability)

An Ability making its debut in Generation IX is Lingering Aroma, known in Japanese as とれないにおい (Lingering Scent). This is exclusively the signature Ability of male Oinkologne. When a Pokémon with Lingering Aroma is struck by a contact move, the attacking Pokémon's Ability transforms into Lingering Aroma. The aggressor's original Ability is restored upon being switched out, fainting, or the battle concluding. Should a Pokémon possessing this Ability be hit by a contact multistrike move (such as Fury Swipes), the attacking Pokémon's Ability will become Lingering Aroma following the initial strike. If a Pokémon with Rock Head executes a recoil contact move against a Pokémon with Lingering Aroma, its Ability will first change to Lingering Aroma, after which it will incur recoil damage. Lingering Aroma does not affect Multitype, Zen Mode, Stance Change, Shields Down, Schooling, Disguise, Battle Bond, Power Construct, Comatose, RKS System, Gulp Missile, Ice Face, As One, Zero to Hero, Commander, Tera Shift, Mummy, or Lingering Aroma itself. In the sequential order of index numbers, Lingering Aroma holds the distinction of being the first Generation IX Ability. Lingering Aroma stands as the sole signature Ability specifically tied to one gender of its species. Female Oinkologne, on the other hand, may possess the Ability Aroma Veil, a trait shared with its pre-evolved form. This gender-specific nature of Lingering Aroma for male Oinkologne likely serves as an homage to how real-life male pigs, upon reaching puberty, develop a gland producing an odor called boar taint, a scent and gland absent in female pigs.

Title: Seed Sower (Ability)

An Ability making its debut in Generation IX, Seed Sower (こぼれダネ, translated as Self-Sowing Seeds, in Japanese) is a distinctive power. It serves as Arboliva's unique signature Ability. When a Pokémon benefiting from Seed Sower takes a hit from any damaging attack, it brings forth Grassy Terrain, lasting for five turns, unless that terrain type is already established. Equipping the Pokémon with a Terrain Extender can stretch this effect to eight turns. For multi-strike attacks, activation occurs on the initial strike. Crucially, Seed Sower triggers prior to the effects of the moves Steel Roller and Ice Spinner taking place, resulting in the immediate removal of the Grassy Terrain that was just summoned.

Title: Thermal Exchange (Ability)

Introduced in Generation IX, Thermal Exchange (Japanese: ねつこうかん Thermal Exchange) is an Ability that belongs exclusively to the evolutionary line of Frigibax. When a Pokémon with this Ability is struck by a damaging move of the Fire type, its Attack stat will increase by one stage. This boost occurs without providing any immunity to or reduction of the incoming damage. Additionally, it prevents the Pokémon from becoming burned. The Ability's effect will not trigger if a Substitute takes the hit. Furthermore, if a Pokémon having Thermal Exchange becomes burned during battle (for instance, if it obtained the Ability while already burned outside of battle, through an effect like Skill Swap, or was burned by a Pokémon with an Ability such as Mold Breaker), it will instantly be cured of the burn.

Title: Anger Shell (Ability)

Debuting in Generation IX, Anger Shell (Japanese: いかりのこうら Anger Shell) is an Ability exclusively possessed by Klawf. This unique capability is triggered when the Pokémon's HP is lowered from above 50% to 50% or less, specifically as a consequence of an attack launched by a foe. Upon activation, its Attack, Special Attack, and Speed each ascend by one stage, while concurrently, its Defense and Special Defense each descend by one stage. It is crucial to note that damage from non-attack sources, such as status conditions, recoil, or the Life Orb, will not cause Anger Shell to activate. Furthermore, when the Pokémon is hit by a multistrike move, the Ability's effect will only apply after all individual strikes have been completed.

Title: Purifying Salt (Ability)

Introduced in Generation IX, the Ability known as Purifying Salt (Japanese: きよめのしお Purifying Salt) is the distinct signature trait of Nacli and its evolved forms. A Pokémon possessing Purifying Salt gains complete immunity to all non-volatile status ailments. Furthermore, when a Ghost-type move targets the Pokémon, the attacking Pokémon's Attack and Special Attack stats are effectively halved during the damage calculation process. Notably, the move Rest will invariably fail if attempted by a Pokémon with this Ability. Should a Pokémon become afflicted with a status condition *before* acquiring Purifying Salt, the condition persists and is not nullified upon the Ability's activation. The mechanism by which Purifying Salt diminishes damage from Ghost-type assaults likely draws inspiration from Japanese folklore, where salt is revered for its purifying qualities, acting as a cleanser and a deterrent against malevolent spirits. Its protective influence against status conditions, moreover, might allude to the historical uses of salt in various remedies and as a safeguard against illnesses, a practice observed notably among the ancient civilizations of Egypt and Greece.

Title: Wind Rider (Ability)

Making its debut in Generation IX, Wind Rider (Japanese: かぜのり Wind Riding) is an Ability that bestows particular advantages. A Pokémon bearing Wind Rider completely negates damage from wind-based attacks. Moreover, its Attack stat will elevate by one stage if it is hit by such a move. The activation of Tailwind on the Pokémon's side of the field, or bringing the Wind Rider Pokémon into battle while Tailwind is already in effect there, will also cause its Attack to surge by one stage. This bonus applies on top of the typical speed enhancement Tailwind provides. Notably, Sandstorm, despite its classification as a wind move, is unique in that it never interacts with Wind Rider, a characteristic stemming from its field-targeting nature. Before Generation IX, the Pokémon Shiftry possessed the Early Bird Ability rather than Wind Rider.

Title: Guard Dog (Ability)

Guard Dog (Japanese: ばんけん Guard Dog) debuted in Generation IX. This Ability provides immunity against external forces attempting to compel the Pokémon to switch out or flee. Such attempts, whether from moves like Roar or Circle Throw, or items such as Red Card, will be nullified. However, Guard Dog does not impede the Pokémon's self-initiated departures. The Pokémon can still switch out manually, or use its own moves (e.g., Baton Pass, Teleport) or items (Eject Button, Eject Pack) to leave the battle. Furthermore, when a Pokémon with Guard Dog is affected by Intimidate, its Attack stat uniquely rises by one stage, rather than falling by one stage.

Title: Wind Power (Ability)

The Ability known as Wind Power (Japanese: ふうりょくでんき Wind-Powered Electricity) made its debut in Generation IX. It functions as the exclusive signature skill of the Pokémon Wattrel and Kilowattrel. A Pokémon possessing Wind Power becomes charged, thereby augmenting the power of its subsequent Electric-type move, either when it's targeted by a wind move or when the effects of Tailwind come into play. Upon this Ability's activation, the game displays the message "Being hit by <move> charged <name> with power!", and this notification appears even if the triggering event causes the Pokémon with Wind Power to faint. Should an opposing wind move be the cause of the Pokémon's fainting, the Wind Power message will be shown prior to its collapse. Notably, Sandstorm is the solitary exception among wind moves that fails to interact with Wind Power, a peculiarity stemming from its field-targeting nature.

Title: Commander (Ability)

For information regarding the Trainer class, refer to Commander (Trainer class). Known in Japanese as しれいとう Commander, this Ability made its debut in Generation IX. It serves as Tatsugiri's exclusive Ability. Should a Tatsugiri with Commander occupy the same side of the battlefield as a Dondozo, it will proceed to enter Dondozo's mouth, resulting in Dondozo's Attack, Defense, Special Attack, Special Defense, and Speed stats each increasing by two stages. As Tatsugiri remains within Dondozo's mouth, Dondozo itself becomes incapable of switching out (even if Tatsugiri faints) and cannot be compelled to leave the battle. Although a held Red Card can still be used up, it will yield no outcome. The Trainer loses the ability to choose moves for Tatsugiri, and any opposing attacks will miss if Tatsugiri is the target, regardless of whether the attacking Pokémon possesses No Guard. Tatsugiri persists in taking damage from sandstorms and existing status conditions (like poison) acquired before its entry into Dondozo's mouth; the effects of Perish Song similarly proceed as normal. Should Dondozo be brought into battle while Tatsugiri is already present, Commander immediately activates, canceling Tatsugiri's chosen move. Any attacks aimed at Tatsugiri that turn will also miss. Upon Dondozo fainting, Tatsugiri reverts to its standard battle stance. Commander does not re-engage if Tatsugiri faints and is subsequently replaced by another Tatsugiri possessing Commander. Nevertheless, the Ability can be reactivated if Dondozo is revived following its faint. Using the move Order Up grants Dondozo a stat increase determined by the specific form of Tatsugiri currently within its mouth: Curly Form Tatsugiri provides a one-stage boost to Attack. Droopy Form Tatsugiri raises Defense by one stage. Stretchy Form Tatsugiri elevates Speed by one stage. This Ability remains inactive during Multi Battles and Tera Raid Battles. Both Gastro Acid and Worry Seed will fail to affect a target if it possesses the Commander Ability. Moves such as Role Play, Skill Swap, Entrainment, and Doodle are unsuccessful if Commander is held by either participant. Abilities like Trace, Power of Alchemy, and Receiver are unable to replicate Commander. However, Simple Beam can replace it. Lingering Aroma is incapable of overwriting Commander. An Imposter-user can successfully Transform into a Tatsugiri that is inside Dondozo's mouth. Should Dondozo possess the Contrary Ability, its stats will be decreased rather than increased. Within Pokémon Legends: Z-A, Abilities are not present during standard gameplay. Nevertheless, if Dondozo enters a battle with a non-Mega-Evolved, non-fainted Tatsugiri also in the party, Tatsugiri will move into Dondozo's mouth, enhancing all of Dondozo's stats and making it impossible to recall until the battle concludes. In situations where multiple eligible Tatsugiri exist within the party, Dondozo will consume the leftmost one according to party order.

Title: Electromorphosis (Ability)

Electromorphosis (Japanese: でんきにかえる, meaning "Change into Electricity") is an Ability that first appeared in Generation IX. Bellibolt uniquely possesses this as its signature capability. Upon being struck by any move, a Pokémon with Electromorphosis enters a "charged" state, which subsequently boosts the power of the next Electric-type move it unleashes. Should the Pokémon be subjected to a multistrike attack, each individual hit will activate the Ability's effect; however, these charges do not accumulate. When Electromorphosis triggers, the system displays the message: "Being hit by <move> charged <name> with power!" This notification appears regardless of whether the incoming move causes the Electromorphosis user to faint. Indeed, if the opposing attack leads to the Pokémon's incapacitation, this message is presented prior to its fainting animation. The Japanese name for this Ability, かえる (kaeru), incorporates a clever double meaning: it can be interpreted as the verb 変える, signifying "to change," or as the noun 蛙, referring to a "frog." This linguistic play likely accounts for its exclusive association with Bellibolt, the "EleFrog Pokémon." The English designation, Electromorphosis, is a portmanteau formed from "electro-" and "metamorphosis." During Showdown! The Paldea Elite Four, Jacq elucidated Electromorphosis as Bellibolt's method for generating and retaining electrical energy after its abdominal muscles vibrate from an impact.

Title: Protosynthesis (Ability)

Known in Japanese as こだいかっせい (Ancient Activation), Protosynthesis debuted as an Ability in Generation IX. It serves as the exclusive Ability for most ancient Paradox Pokémon, with Koraidon being the sole exception. This Ability activates under specific conditions: either when the Pokémon is exposed to harsh sunlight or when it carries a Booster Energy item. Upon activation, its highest stat – excluding HP, and factoring in current stat stages but not held items – receives a boost. This increase is 30% for any stat, or a more significant 50% if Speed is the stat that's highest. Once Protosynthesis triggers, a notification will inform all players about which particular stat has been enhanced. Should multiple stats be equally high, Protosynthesis resolves such ties using a predefined priority order: Attack, then Defense, followed by Special Attack, Special Defense, and finally Speed.

Harsh sunlight will still trigger Protosynthesis even if the Pokémon holds a Utility Umbrella. However, the Ability will not activate if another Pokémon with Air Lock or Cloud Nine is present on the battlefield. Notably, harsh sunlight takes precedence over a held Booster Energy for activation purposes. Consequently, if harsh sunlight is active, the Booster Energy item will remain unconsumed. When Protosynthesis is brought about by weather conditions, its effects cease once harsh sunlight dissipates from the field.

The stat boost provided by Protosynthesis is not transferable via Baton Pass. Furthermore, attempts to use Skill Swap or Doodle will fail if either Pokémon involved possesses Protosynthesis. Role Play will similarly fail when targeting a Pokémon with Protosynthesis. Nevertheless, Simple Beam, Worry Seed, and Entrainment are effective against it. Protosynthesis is also immune to being copied by Abilities like Receiver, Trace, or Power of Alchemy. Should a Pokémon acquire Protosynthesis through abilities like Imposter or Transform, the acquired Ability will not activate, irrespective of whether harsh sunlight is present or if the Pokémon is holding a Booster Energy.

Without external stat modifications, the maximum possible difference between a Pokémon's base stats that allows Protosynthesis to boost *any* stat is 72 points. This scenario assumes that the stat intended to be lowest receives maximum Effort Values (EVs), 31 Individual Values (IVs), and a beneficial Nature, while the stat intended to be highest has 0 EVs, 0 IVs, and a detrimental Nature. Due to inherent base stat distributions and calculation mechanics, certain Pokémon are unable to receive a Protosynthesis boost for particular stats in battle, even under optimal conditions (i.e., with no external stat changes). This specific calculation considers applying a negative Nature with 0 IVs and 0 EVs to the stat that would naturally be highest, and a positive Nature with 31 IVs and maximum EVs to the stat that would otherwise be unboostable. Specifically:
*   Great Tusk cannot have its Special Attack or Special Defense increased because its Attack and Defense stats will invariably be superior.
*   Brute Bonnet is unable to boost its Speed; its Attack will consistently be higher, except at level 27 or below, but it is unobtainable below level 55.
*   Flutter Mane cannot receive an Attack or Defense boost, as its other stats (Special Attack, Special Defense, and Speed) will always surpass them.
*   Roaring Moon will never have its Special Attack increased due to its Attack stat consistently being higher.

Title: Quark Drive (Ability)

Debuting in Generation IX, the Ability known as Quark Drive (クォークチャージ in Japanese) is the exclusive trait of all futuristic Paradox Pokémon, with Miraidon being the sole exception. This Ability provides a significant boost to the Pokémon's highest non-HP stat when certain conditions are met: either Electric Terrain is in play, or the Pokémon is holding a Booster Energy. The stat increase is 30%, or an even greater 50% if Speed happens to be the stat with the highest value. This calculation considers current stat stages but excludes any benefits from held items. Once activated, a notification is displayed to all participants, indicating which specific stat has been enhanced. Should multiple stats share the highest value, Quark Drive resolves the tie according to a specific hierarchy: Attack takes precedence, followed by Defense, then Special Attack, Special Defense, and finally Speed. Notably, this effect triggers even if the Pokémon is not grounded. Electric Terrain's presence will prioritize Quark Drive's activation over a held Booster Energy. Consequently, if Electric Terrain is active, the Booster Energy item will not be consumed. When Quark Drive is triggered by terrain, its benefits cease the moment Electric Terrain dissipates from the battlefield.

The stat boosts granted by Quark Drive are explicitly not transferable via Baton Pass. Attempts to use Skill Swap or Doodle will be unsuccessful if either Pokémon involved possesses Quark Drive. Role Play will not affect a target with Quark Drive, though Simple Beam, Worry Seed, and Entrainment remain effective against it. Abilities such as Receiver, Trace, or Power of Alchemy are unable to copy Quark Drive. Should a Pokémon acquire Quark Drive through moves like Imposter or Transform, the Ability's activation conditions (Electric Terrain or Booster Energy) will not trigger its effect. The Ability's nomenclature is derived from 'quarks,' a classification of sub-atomic particles.

For Quark Drive to be able to boost *any* stat without reliance on external modifications, the maximum allowable difference between a Pokémon's individual base stats is 72 points. This calculation assumes the lowest stat is optimized with maximum effort values (EVs), 31 individual values (IVs), and a beneficial Nature, while the highest stat has 0 EVs, 0 IVs, and a hindering Nature. Due to inherent base stat distributions and calculation mechanics, certain Pokémon are inherently unable to receive a Quark Drive boost for specific stats in battle without external stat alterations. This specifically accounts for a negative Nature and 0 IVs/EVs applied to the stat that would naturally be highest, and a positive Nature with 31 IVs and maximum EVs applied to the stat that cannot be boosted. Iron Bundle, for instance, cannot augment its Special Defense because its Speed stat will invariably be superior. Iron Hands will consistently have a higher Attack, precluding any increase to its Special Attack or Speed. Iron Moth's Special Attack will perpetually exceed its Defense, preventing a Defense boost. Finally, Iron Valiant is unable to enhance its Special Defense, as either its Attack or Special Attack will always be the dominant stat.

Title: Orichalcum Pulse (Ability)

First appearing in Generation IX, Orichalcum Pulse (Japanese: ひひいろのこどう Hihiirokane Pulse) is an Ability. It serves as Koraidon's exclusive signature Ability. When a Pokémon with Orichalcum Pulse enters the battle, it immediately calls forth harsh sunlight. This summoned harsh sunlight mirrors the effects of the move Sunny Day, lasting for five turns. This duration can be extended to eight turns if the Pokémon is holding a Heat Rock. Orichalcum Pulse also boosts the Pokémon's Attack stat by roughly 33% (more precisely, by a factor of 5461/4096) while harsh sunlight is active. This Attack increase takes effect even if the Pokémon is equipped with a Utility Umbrella. A notification is displayed upon the Pokémon's entry into battle, even if harsh sunlight is already present. However, contrary to Protosynthesis, no message is shown if harsh sunlight is summoned or dissipates while a Pokémon with Orichalcum Pulse is already engaged. Skill Swap fails if either combatant possesses Orichalcum Pulse. Trace, however, is capable of copying Orichalcum Pulse. Role Play, Entrainment, and Doodle all prove ineffective when used on a target with Orichalcum Pulse. Orichalcum Pulse is susceptible to the influences of Simple Beam, Mummy, and Lingering Aroma. The Ability fails to activate if overworld weather is present. The appellation Orichalcum Pulse refers to orichalcum, a mythological metal found in ancient Greek texts. Its Japanese name, hihiirokane, originates from a legendary metal in Japanese texts, said to be harder than diamonds and never to rust. This term can also be written in kanji as 日緋色金 hihiirokane, translating to "sun-scarlet metal," potentially alluding to the Ability's function of creating harsh sunlight and Koraidon's status as the mascot for Pokémon Scarlet.

Title: Hadron Engine (Ability)

Originating in Generation IX, Hadron Engine (Japanese: ハドロンエンジン Hadron Engine) is a distinct Ability. This particular Ability is unique to the Pokémon Miraidon. Upon a Pokémon possessing Hadron Engine entering the fray, the battlefield immediately manifests the effects of the move Electric Terrain. This Electric Terrain persists for a duration of five turns. Holding a Terrain Extender item will prolong its duration to eight turns. Furthermore, while Electric Terrain is active, Hadron Engine enhances the Pokémon's Special Attack stat by approximately 33%, or more precisely, by a factor of 5461/4096. Notably, this stat increase applies regardless of whether the Pokémon is grounded. A notification for Hadron Engine appears when its user enters battle, even if Electric Terrain is already active. Conversely, if Electric Terrain is initiated while a Hadron Engine Pokémon is already engaged in battle, no such message is shown, unlike with Quark Drive. The move Skill Swap will fail when either participant possesses Hadron Engine. However, Trace is capable of copying Hadron Engine. Attempts to use Role Play, Entrainment, or Doodle on a Pokémon with Hadron Engine will all prove unsuccessful. This Ability is susceptible to the effects of Simple Beam, Mummy, and Lingering Aroma.

Title: Opportunist (Ability)

For the skill found in Pokémon Shuffle, please refer to Skill (Shuffle) → Opportunist. This Ability, known as Opportunist (びんじょう in Japanese), debuted in Generation IX and is the signature Ability of Espathra. When a hostile Pokémon boosts its stats, the Pokémon with Opportunist will mirror these enhancements, raising its corresponding stats by an identical number of stages. This Ability will not activate if an allied Pokémon raises its stats, nor if an opposing Pokémon's stat increase is itself caused by Opportunist. However, Opportunist will trigger for its holder when an ally uses Swagger or Flatter on an adversary, specifically *after* the confusion status has been applied. If multiple triggers occur simultaneously (for example, a Torch Song used by a Pokémon holding Throat Spray), Opportunist will cumulatively apply the stat changes.

Title: Sharpness (Ability)

The Ability known as Sharpness (Japanese: きれあじ Sharpness) made its debut in Generation IX. When a Pokémon possesses Sharpness, the power of its slicing moves increases by 50%. A comprehensive list of moves that are impacted by Sharpness, along with the Pokémon capable of acquiring Sharpness and learning those particular moves, is provided in the subsequent table. Despite being influenced by this Ability, certain moves listed below cannot presently be learned by any Pokémon that naturally has Sharpness. Nevertheless, these moves can still manifest through actions like Metronome, Copycat, or Mimic, or be executed by a Pokémon that acquired Sharpness via an Ability like Trace or Receiver, or through a move such as Skill Swap or Role Play. Within the internal programming of Pokémon Legends: Arceus, Hisuian Samurott's Hidden Ability is identified as Shell Armor, not Sharpness. Similarly, Kleavor's Hidden Ability is designated as Steadfast, rather than Sharpness. The English names of several slicing moves, which diverge from their Japanese counterparts, unfortunately obscure the rationale behind their classification as such. For instance, Aerial Ace's Japanese name, つばめがえし (Swallow Return), directly references a traditional sword technique. Similarly, Population Bomb is known as ネズミざん (Nezumizan) in Japanese, a term ingeniously playable as both ねずみ算 (nezumizan), signifying "to multiply like mice" – literally "mouse mathematics" and a familiar arithmetic challenge – and ねずみ斬 (nezumizan), meaning "mouse cut."

Title: Supreme Overlord (Ability)

Supreme Overlord, designated そうだいしょう Supreme Commander in Japan, made its debut as an Ability in Generation IX. It is the exclusive signature trait of Kingambit. Upon entering a battle, a Pokémon with Supreme Overlord enjoys an additive 10% enhancement to the power of its attacks. This bonus accrues for every ally Pokémon in its party that has already fainted. Similarly, the Pokémon Conquest Abilities "Hero" (おそれしらず Fearless) and "Last Bastion" (さいごのとりで Final Fortress) offer comparable mechanics. These grant their user boosts to their Attack and Defense stats, determined by the number of defeated party members currently under the player's command.

Title: Toxic Debris (Ability)

Known in Japanese as どくげしょう (Scattered Poison), Toxic Debris made its debut as an Ability in Generation IX. This particular Ability is unique to the Pokémon Glimmet and Glimmora. Should a Pokémon possessing Toxic Debris sustain damage from a physical attack, a layer of Toxic Spikes will automatically be deployed on the opponent's side of the battle arena. However, the Ability will not trigger if the incoming attack would result in more than two layers of Toxic Spikes being placed, or if the hit connects with a substitute rather than the Pokémon itself. Furthermore, in instances where a Pokémon equipped with this Ability is struck by a physical multistrike move (for example, Fury Swipes), every individual strike will separately activate Toxic Debris. Any statistics presented herein reflect exact values, not merely base stats. These values are explicitly defined rather than being calculated from standard factors like base stats, level, Nature, IVs, and EVs.

Title: Armor Tail (Ability)

Armor Tail (Japanese: テイルアーマー Tail Armor) is an Ability first introduced in Generation IX, serving as the signature Ability of Farigiraf. When an opponent uses a high-priority move (including those boosted by Prankster, Gale Wings, or Triage) that targets the Armor Tail user or its allies, the Ability prevents the move's execution, though its PP is still deducted. Consequently, opponents can only target the Pokémon with Armor Tail or its allies with moves of standard or decreased priority.

However, Armor Tail offers no protection against moves that target all Pokémon (except Perish Song) or those that target the opponent's side of the field, even if such moves possess increased priority. It also has no effect on increased priority moves used by the Pokémon's allies. Abilities like Mold Breaker, Turboblaze, and Teravolt are capable of ignoring Armor Tail.

Moves with increased priority, when called via Instruct, retain their original priority and are blocked by Armor Tail. Conversely, moves with decreased or standard priority called by an increased-priority Instruct (e.g., from a Prankster user) similarly retain their original priority and are not blocked. Armor Tail cannot block increased priority moves that are invoked by any other type of 'calling move'. Nevertheless, if a 'calling move' itself is used with increased priority, Armor Tail *will* block the subsequent called move, regardless of its inherent priority.

Title: Earth Eater (Ability)

Making its debut in Generation IX, Earth Eater (どしょく Geophagy in Japanese) is an Ability exclusively held by Orthworm. Should a Pokémon possessing Earth Eater be struck by a Ground-type attack, it will regain hit points equivalent to one quarter of its maximum HP. Furthermore, the Ground-type move will be entirely negated, having no effect on the Pokémon. This remains true even if the Pokémon's HP is already completely full, in which case the Ground-type technique performs no action. It is important to note that Earth Eater will not trigger if the Pokémon is safeguarded from the Ground-type move. Documentation in PASV18 explicitly states that the Titan Orthworm was equipped with the Earth Eater Ability.

Title: Mycelium Might (Ability)

Known in Japanese as きんしのちから (Hyphal Power), Mycelium Might is an Ability that made its debut in Generation IX. It serves as the unique Ability for both Toedscool and its evolution, Toedscruel. When a Pokémon possessing Mycelium Might initiates a status move, two specific conditions apply: the move will always resolve last among others of the same priority level, and crucially, any ignorable Abilities belonging to any Pokémon on the field are disregarded during that move's execution. To clarify, ignorable Abilities are primarily those that could hinder a move's effectiveness, damage output, or overall impact if present on the target Pokémon or their allies. For instance, should a Pokémon with Mycelium Might employ Screech, it would execute the move at the end of its priority class, but would nonetheless be able to affect foes equipped with Abilities like Big Pecks, Clear Body, or Soundproof.

Title: Toxic Chain (Ability)

If you're seeking the Japanese move also known as Toxic Chain, please refer to Malignant Chain (move). Toxic Chain (Japanese: どくのくさり Toxic Chain) is an Ability that was introduced in Generation IX, making its debut in The Teal Mask expansion. This Ability is exclusive to the Loyal Three. When a Pokémon possessing Toxic Chain executes any move that is not a status move, there exists a 30% probability that the opposing Pokémon will become badly poisoned. This 30% activation chance for Toxic Chain operates independently for every individual hit of a multistrike move. Should this Ability trigger when Knock Off is used against a foe holding either a Lum Berry or a Pecha Berry, the Berry will be consumed to cure the inflicted poisoning, rather than being dislodged by Knock Off's usual effect. A physical Toxic Chain can be observed encircling Okidogi's neck, Munkidori's head, and Fezandipiti's waist; these three are the only Pokémon known to possess this Ability. Additionally, two Toxic Chains are distinctly visible during the animation of Pecharunt's signature move, Malignant Chain, an attack whose Japanese name is nearly identical to this Ability's.

Title: Embody Aspect (Ability)

Embody Aspect, known in Japanese as おもかげやどし (Bearing Visage), is an Ability that made its debut in Generation IX as part of The Teal Mask expansion. It functions as the exclusive signature Ability for Ogerpon when it undergoes Terastallization, and its specific effects are contingent upon Ogerpon's current form. Upon Terastallizing, Ogerpon's Ability transforms into Embody Aspect, simultaneously increasing one of its stats by a single stage, with the particular stat boosted being dictated by the mask Ogerpon is wearing. Notably, Embody Aspect shares with Teraform Zero the distinction of being the sole Abilities acquired exclusively through the process of Terastallization. Additionally, it holds the unique characteristic of being the only Ability that cannot be registered in Pokémon HOME.

Title: Tera Shift (Ability)

This Ability, known in Japanese as テラスチェンジ (Tera Change), made its debut during Generation IX, specifically in The Indigo Disk. It serves as one of the exclusive signature Abilities of Terapagos. The moment Terapagos enters combat, it immediately transforms into its Terastal Form, remaining in this state until the battle concludes. Notably, Tera Shift cannot be duplicated by Abilities such as Trace, Power of Alchemy, or Receiver. Furthermore, it is immune to being replaced by Lingering Aroma and cannot be suppressed by Neutralizing Gas. In the context of Auto Battles, Terapagos will first assume its Terastal Form before proceeding to attack the wild Pokémon.

Title: Tera Shell (Ability)

This ability, known as Tera Shell (テラスシェル in Japanese), made its debut in Generation IX as part of The Indigo Disk expansion. It serves as one of Terapagos's distinctive signature Abilities. Should Terapagos endure a damage-dealing attack while at maximum HP (provided the attack isn't already ineffective due to type matchups), the incoming damage will invariably be treated as "not very effective." This "not very effective" status applies to the entirety of the move, extending even to those that strike multiple times. Furthermore, Tera Shell supersedes the effects of Tar Shot. While Tera Shell offers no protection against moves that inflict direct damage, Struggle, or self-inflicted confusion damage, it notably *does* influence typeless Revelation Dance. Nevertheless, for those aforementioned direct damage sources, the game still presents the message "It's not very effective...", despite the damage reduction not actually occurring. Uniquely within Pokémon Scarlet and Violet, Tera Shell provides the sole means for a Pokémon to experience resisted damage when struck by Stellar-type moves.

Title: Teraform Zero (Ability)

This Ability, known in Japan as ゼロフォーミング (Zero-Forming), made its debut in Generation IX with The Indigo Disk expansion. It is recognized as one of Terapagos's distinctive signature Abilities. The moment Terapagos adopts its Stellar Form, all active weather and terrain effects are instantaneously cleared. Like other Abilities, Teraform Zero is susceptible to suppression from specific moves, including Gastro Acid, and Abilities such as Neutralizing Gas, which function by inhibiting other powers. Furthermore, its presence can be overwritten by alternative Abilities through the application of Entrainment, Worry Seed, or Doodle. Should physical contact be made with a foe possessing Mummy, Wandering Spirit, or Lingering Aroma, Teraform Zero will subsequently convert into the opponent's respective Ability. However, attempts to duplicate Teraform Zero using Trace or Role Play are unsuccessful, nor can it be gained via Skill Swap, Power of Alchemy, or Receiver. Considering the distinct mechanics of Generation IX's overworld weather, Teraform Zero offers no defense against its environmental repercussions. Alongside Embody Aspect, Teraform Zero stands as one of just two Abilities exclusively attained via Terastallization. Notably, its French and Spanish localizations are unique among all Ability names for incorporating a numeral, with both versions featuring '0'.

Title: Poison Puppeteer (Ability)

This Ability, known as Poison Puppeteer (Japanese: どくくぐつ Poison Puppeteer), made its debut in Generation IX's The Indigo Disk, though it became accessible only upon Mochi Mayhem's launch. It is the signature Ability exclusively belonging to Pecharunt. When a Pokémon is poisoned through any of Pecharunt's moves, it will simultaneously become confused. Notably, poison inflicted by Toxic Spikes does not activate Poison Puppeteer. Furthermore, for Poison Puppeteer to take effect, the user must specifically be Pecharunt. Skill Swap invariably fails if either Pokémon involved possesses Poison Puppeteer. Additionally, Power of Alchemy is unable to copy Poison Puppeteer. It holds the distinction of being the last Generation IX Ability in numerical index order.
